It "just works" on macOS and Linux without runtime dependencies.
> 
> The `npx create-youmd` path handles scaffolding + interactive onboarding (prompts for username, source URLs, etc.) and is the smoothest path for Node.js users.
> 
> Both paths converge on the same CLI binary and the same onboarding flow.
> 
> **CLI is the primary onboarding path.** The web app onboarding is a secondary path — it runs the same pipeline with the same steps, just rendered as a visual UI instead of terminal prompts. The web path exists for users who don't live in a terminal, but the default assumption is CLI-first.
> 
> ```
> youmd <command> [options]
> 
> Core Commands:
>   init                    Initialize a new You.md bundle locally (no account needed)
>   login                   Authenticate with you.md platform
>   register                Create account + claim username
>   add <source> <url>      Add a source (website, linkedin, x, blog, youtube, github)
>   build                   Run ingestion pipeline + compile bundle
>   preview                 Preview compiled profile locally (opens local dev server)
>   diff                    Show changes since last publish
>   publish                 Push bundle to you.md/<username> (requires account)
>   status                  Show pipeline/build status
> 
> Key Management:
>   keys list               List API keys
>   keys create             Create new API key
>   keys revoke <id>        Revoke API key
> 
> Context Links:
>   link create             Create a shareable context link
>   link create --scope=full   Include private context (Pro only)
>   link create --ttl=24h      Set expiry (1h, 24h, 7d, 30d, 90d, never)
>   link list               List active context links
>   link revoke <id>        Revoke a context link
>   link revoke --all       Revoke all context links
> 
> Configuration:
>   config                  View all CLI config
>   config set <key> <val>  Set a config value
>   config get <key>        Get a config value
> 
>   # BYOK keys (Pro only)
>   config set openrouter-key <key>
>   config set perplexity-key <key>
>   config set apify-key <key>
>   config set firecrawl-key <key>
> 
> Skill Export:
>   skill export            Output the youmd skill file to stdout
>   skill export --format=cursor   Export as .cursorrules format
> 
> Utility:
>   whoami                  Show current authenticated user
>   logout                  Clear local auth
> 
> Options:
>   --json                  Output as JSON (for scripting)
>   --verbose               Show detailed output
>   --dry-run               Preview without writing
>   --local                 Force local-only mode (no network calls)
>   --help                  Show help
> ```
> 
> **CLI implementation details:**
> 
> - Written in TypeScript.
> - **Two distribution paths:**
>   - npm package (`youmd`) — for Node.js users. `npx create-youmd` for scaffolding, `npm install -g youmd` for global install.
>   - Standalone binary — compiled via `bun build --compile` (or `pkg`). Distributed via `curl -fsSL https://you.md/install.sh | sh`. Zero runtime dependencies. macOS + Linux. Windows support via WSL initially.
> - Uses `commander` for argument parsing.
> - Uses `ink` or raw ANSI for terminal UI (minimal — no unnecessary animation).
> - Auth tokens stored in `~/.youmd/config.json`.
> - BYOK API keys stored in `~/.youmd/config.json` (never sent to platform server).
> - Local bundle stored in `.youmd/` directory in the project root.
> - **Local-first:** `youmd init` and `youmd build --local` work with no account and no network calls (builds bundle from manually authored files only). Pipeline ingestion (scraping + LLM analysis) requires either platform auth (free tier) or BYOK keys (Pro).
> - All platform network calls go through the same REST API that the web UI uses. The CLI is a thin client.
> - BYOK keys are passed directly to third-party APIs at call time — they never transit through the You.md backend.
> 
> **`npx create-youmd` interactive flow:**
> 
> ```
> $ npx create-youmd
> 
>   you.md — your identity file for the agent internet
> 
>   ? Choose a username: houston
>   ✓ houston is available
> 
>   ? Your website URL (optional): https://houstongolden.com
>   ? Your LinkedIn URL (optional): https://linkedin.com/in/houstongolden
>   ? Your X/Twitter URL (optional): https://x.com/houstongolden
> 
>   Building your identity bundle...
>   ├── Discovering content via Perplexity Sonar
>   ├── Scraping website via Firecrawl
>   ├── Scraping LinkedIn via Apify
>   ├── Extracting structured data
>   ├── Analyzing voice + topics
>   └── Compiling bundle
> 
>   ✓ Bundle ready. Preview:
> 
>   Houston Golden
>   Founder, BAMF Media. Building You.md.
>   Miami, FL
> 
>   ? Publish to you.md/houston? (Y/n): Y
> 
>   ✓ Live at https://you.md/houston
>   ✓ Context link: https://you.md/ctx/houston/abc123def456
>     Paste this into any AI conversation to share your context.
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 5. Product Surfaces
> 
> ### 5.1 Web: Public Profile Page
> 
> ```
> https://you.md/<username>
> ```
> 
> This is a server-rendered page that displays the public identity bundle. It is NOT a page builder. It is a structured, minimal rendering of `you.json`.
> 
> **Layout:**
> - Name, tagline, location
> - Current focus (now)
> - Projects list
> - Values
> - Links
> - "Powered by You.md" footer with link to claim your own
> 
> **Design system:**
> - Black and white. Neutral grays for secondary text.
> - Monospace for headings. System sans-serif for body.
> - 1px borders. Tight spacing. No decorative elements.
> - Dark mode default. Light mode optional.
> - Mobile-responsive (single column).
> 
> ### 5.2 Web: Onboarding + Editor / Dashboard
> 
> **Web onboarding is the secondary path.** It mirrors the CLI onboarding flow step-for-step, rendered as a visual UI:
> 
> 1. Claim username
> 2. Add source URLs (website, LinkedIn, X, etc.)
> 3. Pipeline runs (with real-time progress via Convex reactive queries)
> 4. Review generated bundle (diff view)
> 5. Approve + publish
> 
> This exists for users who don't live in a terminal — founders, creators, marketers. The pipeline, prompts, and output are identical to the CLI path. The only difference is the interface.
> 
> **Authenticated dashboard (post-onboarding):**
> 
> - Edit profile content (structured form, not freeform markdown editor)
> - Add/remove sources
> - Trigger rebuild
> - Review pipeline output (diff view)
> - Approve + publish
> - Manage API keys
> - Create/revoke context links
> - View/edit private vault (Pro)
> 
> **Not in v1:** Custom themes, page builder, drag-and-drop, media uploads.
> 
> ### 5.3 API
> 
> As defined in §4.5. The API is the backbone. Both the CLI and the web UI are clients of the same API.
> 
> ### 5.4 CLI
> 
> As defined in §4.6. The CLI is the primary interface for developer users.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 6. Milestones & Scope
> 
> ### Milestone 0: Foundation (Weeks 1–3)
> 
> **Goal:** Core infrastructure. Auth. Username claim. Empty bundle creation.
> 
> **Ship:**
> - [ ] PostgreSQL schema deployed
> - [ ] API server (Hono/Fastify) with auth (Clerk or Auth.js)
> - [ ] `POST /auth/register` — create user + claim username
> - [ ] `GET /profiles/:username` — return 404 or empty profile
> - [ ] Basic Next.js app with auth flow
> - [ ] Username claim page (check availability, reserve)
> - [ ] `youmd init` and `youmd login` CLI commands
> - [ ] CI/CD pipeline, staging environment
> 
> **Not in scope:** Ingestion, analysis, publishing, public profiles.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Milestone 1: Manual Identity Creation (Weeks 4–6)
> 
> **Goal:** Users can create and publish an identity bundle manually (no scraping yet).
> 
> **Ship:**
> - [ ] Structured profile editor (web form → bundle)
> - [ ] `PUT /me/bundle` — save bundle
> - [ ] `POST /me/publish` — publish bundle
> - [ ] Public profile page at `you.md/<username>` (SSR from `you.json`)
> - [ ] `youmd build` (local compile only, no ingestion)
> - [ ] `youmd publish`
> - [ ] `you.json` and `you.md` compilation from form data
> - [ ] Manifest generation
> 
> **Not in scope:** Scraping, LLM analysis, private vault, API keys.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Milestone 2: Ingestion Pipeline (Weeks 7–10)
> 
> **Goal:** Users can add source URLs and the system scrapes, extracts, and generates analysis.
> 
> **Ship:**
> - [ ] `POST /me/sources` — add source URL
> - [ ] Ingestion pipeline (all 6 stages from §4.4)
> - [ ] Job queue (BullMQ or Inngest)
> - [ ] Website scraping (Firecrawl)
> - [ ] LinkedIn scraping (Apify)
> - [ ] X scraping (Apify)
> - [ ] LLM extraction prompts (per source type)
> - [ ] LLM analysis prompts (voice, topics, bio variants, arcs, FAQ)
> - [ ] Diff review UI (web)
> - [ ] `youmd add <source> <url>`
> - [ ] `youmd build` (now triggers full pipeline)
> - [ ] `youmd diff`
> - [ ] Human-in-the-loop approval before publish
> 
> **Not in scope:** Auto-refresh, interview mode, private vault.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Milestone 3: Security + Sharing + Monetization (Weeks 11–13)
> 
> **Goal:** Private vault. Context links. API keys. Pro plan.
> 
> **Ship:**
> - [ ] Private vault encryption (AES-256-GCM)
> - [ ] `GET/PUT /me/private`
> - [ ] **Context links — create, list, revoke (CLI + web)**
> - [ ] **Context link endpoint: `GET /ctx/:username/:token`**
> - [ ] **Public + full scope support for context links**
> - [ ] API key management (create, list, revoke)
> - [ ] Scoped API keys (`read:public`, `read:private`)
> - [ ] Rate limiting (per plan)
> - [ ] Stripe integration for Pro plan
> - [ ] Pro gating (vault, full-scope context links, scoped keys, higher limits)
> 
> **Not in scope:** MCP, interview mode, team bundles, verified badges.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Milestone 4: Polish + Launch (Weeks 14–16)
> 
> **Goal:** Production-ready. Public launch.
> 
> **Ship:**
> - [ ] Public landing page (you.md)
> - [ ] Spec documentation site (spec.you.md)
> - [ ] CLI published to npm
> - [ ] Error handling, edge cases, loading states
> - [ ] Monitoring + alerting (Sentry, uptime)
> - [ ] Rate limiting hardening
> - [ ] SEO for profile pages
> - [ ] Open Graph / social cards for profiles
> - [ ] `youmd` npm package README + docs
> - [ ] Open spec `you-md/v1` published to GitHub
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Post-Launch Roadmap (Not in v1 scope)
> 
> These are planned but NOT committed. Listed for architectural awareness only.
> 
> | Feature | Earliest | Dependency |
> |---|---|---|
> | Interview mode (`youmd interview`) | v1.1 | Pipeline stable |
> | MCP endpoint (`mcp.you.md/<username>`) | v1.1 | API stable |
> | Custom domains | v1.1 | DNS + Vercel config |
> | Profile analytics (views, agent reads) | v1.1 | API stable |
> | **Verified badges (people)** | **v1.1** | **Identity verification flow defined** |
> | **Verified badges (businesses/orgs)** | **v1.2** | **Business verification flow defined** |
> | Autonomous refresh (`youmd refresh`) | v1.2 | Approval flow stable |
> | Voice onboarding | v1.2 | Interview mode |
> | Identity network directory | v1.2 | Critical mass (~1,000 profiles) |
> | Profile page theming | v1.2+ | Standardized design proven |
> | Newsletter subscribe embed | v1.2+ | Profile page stable |
> | Team/org bundles | v2.0 | Multi-tenant architecture |
> | Self-host export | v2.0 | Spec finalized |
> | Plugin marketplace | v2.0+ | Ecosystem traction |
> 
> ### Verified Badges (v1.1 — Coming Soon)
> 
> Verification is critical to the AEO/GEO thesis. If agents are going to cite You.md profiles as authoritative, there must be a trust signal that the profile actually belongs to the person it claims to represent.
> 
> **Verified Person Badge:**
> - Proves this You.md profile is controlled by the actual person
> - Verification methods (tiered, explore during v1.1 design):
>   - Domain verification (prove you control the website listed in your profile)
>   - Social account verification (OAuth link to LinkedIn, X, GitHub)
>   - DNS TXT record verification (add a TXT record to your domain)
> - Badge displays on public profile page and in `you.json` as a `verified` field
> - Agents consuming `you.json` can check the `verified` flag to assess source reliability
> 
> **Verified Business/Organization Badge:**
> - Proves this You.md profile represents a legitimate business entity
> - Higher bar: may require domain verification + business email + manual review
> - Enables future org-level features (team bundles, org identity at `org.you.md`)
> - Separate badge from personal verification
> 
> **Spec impact:** The `you.json` schema should reserve a `verification` field from v1, even if it's always `null` until v1.1:
> 
> ```jsonc
> {
>   "verification": {
>     "status": "verified" | "unverified",
>     "type": "person" | "business" | null,
>     "methods": ["domain", "linkedin", "github"],
>     "verified_at": "2026-05-01T00:00:00Z"
>   }
> }
> ```
> 
> This field is reserved in the v1 spec but not populated until the verification system ships.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 7. Security & Privacy
> 
> ### 7.1 Principles
> 
> - Private data is encrypted at rest. Always.
> - API keys are hashed. Never stored in plaintext.
> - Scoped access. No API key gets blanket access.
> - Audit logging for all write operations.
> - Users can delete their data completely (hard delete, not soft).
> 
> ### 7.2 Encryption
> 
> - Algorithm: AES-256-GCM
> - Key derivation: Per-user key derived from a master key + user ID (using HKDF)
> - IV: Randomly generated per encryption operation, stored alongside ciphertext
> - At-rest: Private vault (`private.md`, `private.json`) encrypted before write
> 
> **Future (v2+):** User-controlled encryption keys (bring your own key). This is architecturally complex and deferred deliberately.
> 
> ### 7.3 API Key Security
> 
> - Keys are generated as 32-byte random values, prefixed with `ym_` for identification
> - Only the hash (SHA-256) is stored in the database
> - The plaintext key is shown to the user exactly once at creation time
> - Keys support scopes: `read:public`, `read:private`, `write:bundle`
> - Keys can be revoked instantly
> 
> ### 7.4 Data Deletion
> 
> - `DELETE /me` triggers full account deletion
> - All bundles, sources, analysis, keys, and vault data are hard-deleted
> - Object storage files are purged within 24 hours
> - Username is released after 30-day hold (prevents squatting on deletion)
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 8. Go-to-Market & Business
> 
> ### 8.1 Positioning
> 
> **You.md is your identity file for the agent internet.**
> 
> It is infrastructure. The profile page is a byproduct that happens to look great. The value proposition is: every agent you use can now read a canonical, structured representation of who you are, and you control it.
> 
> The mental model: `soul.md` gives agents identity. `agent.md` gives agents instructions. `you.md` gives agents context about the human. It completes the handshake.
> 
> **Target users (in order of priority):**
> 
> 1. **AI-native developers** — people already using Claude Code, OpenClaw, Cursor, and custom agents. They feel the pain of repeating context. They discover via the youmd skill on skills.sh/clawhub.ai or via framework integrations.
> 2. **Founder/creator power users** — people with a strong public presence who want agents to represent them accurately. They discover via seeing someone else's you.md profile page.
> 3. **General knowledge workers** — later. Not the launch audience.
> 
> ### 8.2 Launch Strategy
> 
> 1. **Publish the open spec** on GitHub. This is the credibility move. It signals protocol, not product.
> 2. **Ship the skill to skills.sh and clawhub.ai** on launch day. The skill is the front door.
> 3. **Ship the CLI to npm.** `npx youmd init` should work. Developer credibility comes from the terminal.
> 4. **Submit PRs to 3–5 Tier 1 agent frameworks** in the first two weeks (see §12). Each merged PR is a press release.
> 5. **Launch on Hacker News** with the angle: "We published an open spec for portable human identity for AI agents. Agents have soul.md. Humans need you.md."
> 6. **Launch on Product Hunt** 1–2 weeks after HN, once Tier 1 integrations are live and you can say "already compatible with X, Y, Z."
> 
> ### 8.2.1 The Integration Flywheel
> 
> The integration adoption strategy (§12) is not a nice-to-have — it is the primary growth engine for the first 3 months. The flywheel:
> 
> ```
> Publish spec → PR to small frameworks → "Compatible with You.md" badges
> → More frameworks notice → Larger framework PRs → More users create profiles
> → More profiles = more data in the ecosystem → Frameworks have more reason to support it
> ```
> 
> This is how protocols win. Not by marketing. By being in the dependency tree.
> 
> ### 8.3 Monetization & Tier Model
> 
> #### Design Principles
> 
> 1. **The viral loop must be free.** Creating a bundle, publishing a profile, and sharing a URL must never be gated. That's how You.md grows.
> 2. **Gate on usage intensity, not core functionality.** What costs money is pipeline compute (LLM calls, scraping), private storage (encryption), and API volume (agents consuming profiles at scale). That's where Pro lives.
> 3. **Local-first is free forever.** `youmd init` + `youmd build` should produce a valid bundle on your filesystem with zero network calls and no account. The CLI is a local tool that optionally connects to the platform.
> 
> #### Tier Structure
> 
> | | **Free** | **Pro ($12/mo)** | **Self-Hosted** |
> |---|---|---|---|
> | **Local CLI** | ✓ Full access | ✓ Full access | ✓ Full access |
> | **Local bundle generation** | ✓ (no account needed) | ✓ | ✓ |
> | **Published profile page** | ✓ `you.md/<username>` | ✓ `you.md/<username>` | Self-hosted URL |
> | **Profile SEO/structured data** | ✓ | ✓ | DIY |
> | **Pipeline runs (platform keys)** | 3 total (initial build + 2 refreshes) | 10/month | N/A (BYOK only) |
> | **Source types** | All supported | All supported | All supported |
> | **BYOK (Bring Your Own Keys)** | ✗ | ✓ Unlimited pipeline runs | ✓ Required |
> | **Private encrypted vault** | ✗ | ✓ | Local only (unmanaged) |
> | **Scoped API keys** | 1 key (`read:public` only) | Unlimited keys, all scopes | DIY |
> | **API rate limits** | 30 req/min, 1K/day | 120 req/min, 10K/day | No limits |
> | **Version history** | Latest only | Full history | Local git |
> | **Custom domain** | ✗ | ✓ | N/A |
> | **Auto-refresh** | ✗ | ✓ (when available) | DIY via cron + CLI |
> | **Profile analytics** | ✗ | ✓ (when available) | DIY |
> 
> #### Free vs Paid Logic Explained
> 
> **Why 3 free pipeline runs (not unlimited)?**
> 
> Each pipeline run costs real money: Perplexity Sonar calls (~$0.01–0.05/query), Apify scraper runs (~$0.05–0.15/run), Firecrawl pages (~$0.01/page), and LLM extraction/analysis via OpenRouter (~$0.10–0.50 depending on model and content volume). A full initial build with 3 sources might cost $0.50–1.50 in API calls.
> 
> 3 runs lets a free user: do their initial build (1 run), fix something and rebuild (1 run), and refresh once later (1 run). That's enough for the magic moment and to understand the value. After that, they either go Pro (platform absorbs cost) or bring their own keys.
> 
> **Why BYOK is Pro-only?**
> 
> BYOK configuration adds complexity to the CLI (managing multiple API key types, validating keys, handling mixed platform/user key scenarios). It also means Pro users can run unlimited pipeline rebuilds without costing you anything — which makes Pro more attractive while protecting margins.
> 
> **BYOK Implementation:**
> 
> ```
> youmd config set openrouter-key <key>
> youmd config set perplexity-key <key>
> youmd config set apify-key <key>
> youmd config set firecrawl-key <key>
> ```
> 
> When BYOK keys are configured, the CLI routes API calls through the user's keys instead of platform keys. The platform never stores BYOK keys server-side — they live in `~/.youmd/config.json` on the user's machine and are passed in API request headers at call time.
> 
> #### Self-Hosted Model
> 
> Self-hosting is NOT a supported product in v1. It's an emergent capability of the open spec + local CLI:
> 
> - The spec is public. Anyone can read it and implement a renderer.
> - `youmd init` + `youmd build` work locally with no account. The bundle is just files on disk.
> - A developer can take their local bundle and serve it however they want.
> - The CLI does not include a self-host server or deployment tool in v1.
> 
> **What we document (not build):**
> - "You can self-host your identity bundle by serving the `you/` directory with any static file server."
> - "The `you.json` file is the machine-readable endpoint. Point agents at it."
> - A community guide on self-hosting may emerge. We don't block it, we don't build it.
> 
> **What we build later (v2.0):**
> - `youmd export` — packages the bundle for self-hosting
> - Self-host deployment guide (Vercel, Netlify, Cloudflare Pages)
> - Optional self-host mode in the CLI that skips platform auth
> 
> The goal: self-hosting is *possible* from day one (it's just files), but the hosted platform is so much better that most people won't bother. The open spec earns trust. The hosted platform earns revenue.
> 
> ### 8.4 Success Metrics
> 
> | Timeframe | Metric | Target |
> |---|---|---|
> | Month 1 | CLI installs (npm) | 500 |
> | Month 1 | Profiles created | 200 |
> | Month 1 | GitHub stars (spec repo) | 300 |
> | Month 1 | Skill installs (skills.sh + clawhub.ai) | 200 |
> | Month 1 | Tier 1 framework PRs submitted | 5 |
> | Month 1 | Tier 1 framework PRs merged | 2 |
> | Month 3 | Profiles created | 1,500 |
> | Month 3 | Pro conversions | 150 (10%) |
> | Month 3 | Frameworks with You.md support | 5+ |
> | Month 3 | Tier 2 framework PRs submitted | 3 |
> | Month 6 | Profiles created | 5,000 |
> | Month 6 | MRR | $5,000 |
> | Month 6 | Frameworks with You.md support | 10+ |
> | Month 6 | Tier 3 conversations initiated | 2+ |
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 9. Scope Boundaries: What You.md Is and Isn't
> 
> ### 9.1 You.md Is
> 
> - An open identity file spec (`you-md/v1`)
> - A hosted identity platform with clean, standardized profile pages
> - A CLI-native tool for developers
> - An agent skill for frictionless onboarding
> - Infrastructure for the agent internet
> 
> ### 9.2 You.md Is NOT (v1)
> 
> - **A social network.** No followers, no feed, no DMs, no comments, no engagement loops.
> - **A page builder.** No custom themes, drag-and-drop, or visual customization in v1. Standardized layout ensures quality.
> - **A content platform.** No posts, no articles, no media hosting.
> - **A CRM.** No contact management, no relationship tracking.
> - **A personal wiki.** No freeform pages, no knowledge base.
> - **A competitor to Linktree.** The profile page is a byproduct of the identity bundle, not the product.
> 
> ### 9.3 Future Possibility: Identity Network (v1.2+, Not Committed)
> 
> Long-term, You.md may evolve into an **identity network** — a browsable directory of profiles with analytics (who viewed, which agents consumed your context). This is architecturally supported (the `profileViews` table exists) but is not part of the v1 product or positioning. The v1 message is pure infrastructure.
> 
> If and when a network layer emerges, it will follow these constraints:
> - No feed, no algorithmic distribution
> - No followers/following as a social mechanic
> - Directory/search only — people can find profiles, not "follow" them
> - Profile analytics are private to the profile owner
> 
> The line: people come to *build and share* identity, not to *consume content*.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 10. Skills Distribution Strategy
> 
> ### 10.1 What is a Skill?
> 
> A "skill" is a packaged instruction set that teaches a coding agent (Claude Code, OpenClaw, Codex CLI, etc.) how to work with a tool. The CLI is the tool. The skill is the manual. **The skill is the primary discovery channel for You.md.**
> 
> The typical user doesn't find You.md by searching for identity tools. They find it because:
> 1. They browse skills.sh or clawhub.ai looking for useful agent skills
> 2. They see `youmd` — "Identity file for the agent internet"
> 3. They install the skill
> 4. Their agent walks them through setup
> 
> **This makes the skill the front door and the CLI the engine.**
> 
> ### 10.2 Skill → CLI Relationship
> 
> The skill and CLI are complementary, not redundant. Here's why both are necessary:
> 
> | Capability | Skill alone? | CLI alone? | Skill + CLI |
> |---|---|---|---|
> | Discover You.md | ✓ | ✗ | ✓ |
> | Explain what to do | ✓ | ✗ | ✓ |
> | Auth + username claim | ✗ | ✓ | ✓ |
> | API key management | ✗ | ✓ | ✓ |
> | Trigger ingestion | ✗ | ✓ | ✓ |
> | Build + publish | ✗ | ✓ | ✓ |
> | Guide editing decisions | ✗ | ✗ | ✓ |
> | Review output quality | ✗ | ✗ | ✓ |
> 
> The skill can't handle auth, username claiming, or secure token management — those require a proper client talking to the backend. The CLI can't guide the user conversationally or make editorial judgment calls. Together, the agent (with skill context) drives the CLI and the user gets a guided, intelligent onboarding.
> 
> ### 10.3 The Combined Flow
> 
> ```
> 1. User discovers youmd skill on skills.sh / clawhub.ai
> 2. User installs skill in their coding agent (Claude Code, OpenClaw, etc.)
> 3. User says: "set up my you.md"
> 4. Agent (reading skill):
>    a. Checks if `youmd` CLI is installed
>    b. If not → runs `curl -fsSL https://you.md/install.sh | sh`
>       (or `npx create-youmd` if Node.js is available)
>    c. Walks user through `youmd register` (username + auth)
>    d. Asks user for source URLs conversationally
>    e. Runs `youmd add website <url>`, `youmd add linkedin <url>`, etc.
>    f. Runs `youmd build` → pipeline executes
>    g. Reviews output with user, suggests edits
>    h. Runs `youmd preview` for local review
>    i. User approves → `youmd publish`
> 5. User has a live profile at you.md/<username>
>    + a context link ready to paste into any AI conversation
> ```
> 
> **The skill is the front door. The CLI is the engine. The agent is the guide.**
> 
> ### 10.4 Skill Contents
> 
> The skill file (`.md` format, compatible with skills.sh and clawhub.ai) contains:
> 
> ```markdown
> ---
> name: youmd
> version: 0.1.0
> description: Build and manage your You.md identity bundle — your identity file for the agent internet
> tools: [youmd CLI]
> install: curl -fsSL https://you.md/install.sh | sh
> install_alt: npx create-youmd
> ---
> 
> # You.md Skill
> 
> ## What is You.md?
> You.md is the human side of the agent context handshake.
> Agents have soul.md and agent.md. Humans need you.md.
> It's a structured, portable identity bundle that gives any AI
> agent context about the human it's working for.
> 
> ## Setup
> 1. Check if youmd CLI is installed: `which youmd`
> 2. If not installed:
>    - Preferred: `curl -fsSL https://you.md/install.sh | sh`
>    - If Node.js available: `npx create-youmd`
> 3. Authenticate: `youmd login` (or `youmd register` for new users)
> 
> ## CLI Commands
> [Complete command reference with examples]
> 
> ## Bundle Spec (you-md/v1)
> [Directory structure, required files, key schemas]
> 
> ## Onboarding Guide
> [Conversational flow for helping user add sources, review output, publish]
> 
> ## Editing Bundle Files
> [How to help user refine profile/, preferences/, review analysis/]
> 
> ## Best Practices
> [What makes a good identity bundle, common mistakes, tone guidance]
> ```
> 
> ### 10.5 Distribution Channels
> 
> | Platform | Format | Priority | Ship Target |
> |---|---|---|---|
> | **GitHub repo** | `SKILL.md` in youmd repo | Highest — available immediately | Milestone 1 |
> | **Vercel skills.sh** | `.md` skill file | High — large developer audience | Milestone 4 (launch) |
> | **OpenClaw clawhub.ai** | `.md` skill file | High — exact target user | Milestone 4 (launch) |
> | **Claude Code** | Drop into project as `CLAUDE.md` context | High — manual but effective | Milestone 2 |
> | **Cursor** | `.cursorrules` export via `youmd skill export --format=cursor` | Medium | Post-launch |
> | **Codex CLI** | Prompt config | Medium | Post-launch |
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 11. Viral Loop & Growth Model
> 
> ### 11.1 The Magic Moment
> 
> The magic moment is: **you share your you.md with an agent and it immediately knows you — as if it's been working with you for years.**
> 
> The setup:
> 1. You install the youmd skill or run `youmd init`
> 2. You drop 2–3 URLs (website, LinkedIn, X)
> 3. The pipeline builds your identity bundle — voice profile, bio variants, topic map, narrative arcs, preferences
> 4. You see your profile at `you.md/<username>` — clean, sharp, accurate
> 5. You generate a context link and paste it into a new ChatGPT conversation
> 6. ChatGPT responds as if it already knows your background, your projects, your tone, your preferences
> 
> That's the moment. The agent didn't need onboarding. It didn't need 10 conversations to build memory. It read your you.md and it *got you* immediately.
> 
> **Secondary magic moment:** Someone asks Perplexity "Who is [your name]?" and it returns accurate, current, structured information — pulled from your you.md. Information you control. Information that updates when you update it.
> 
> **The quality bar is non-negotiable.** The ingestion pipeline's output must be impressive on first run. If the voice analysis doesn't sound like the person, or the bio reads like generic LinkedIn filler, the magic moment fails. This means investing heavily in the LLM extraction and analysis prompts — especially voice profiling and bio generation.
> 
> ### 11.2 The Viral Loop
> 
> ```
> CREATE ──────────► MAGIC MOMENT
>                       │
>                       │  "This looks great,
>                       │   I want to share this"
>                       ▼
>                    SHARE ◄──── Profile URL in bio,
>                       │        email signature,
>                       │        social posts,
>                       │        agent instructions
>                       ▼
>                    DISCOVER ◄── Someone clicks a you.md link
>                       │         Sees a great page
>                       │         Sees "Powered by You.md"
>                       ▼
>                    CLAIM ◄───── "I want my you.md/<name>"
>                       │
>                       ▼
>                    CREATE ──────► (repeat)
> ```
> 
> **Key viral properties:**
> 
> - **The URL is inherently shareable.** `you.md/houston` is clean, memorable, brandable. People will put it in bios.
> - **The page is the advertisement.** Every profile page has a subtle "Get your You.md" CTA. The page itself demonstrates the product.
> - **Agent context sharing creates pull.** When someone shares their `you.json` URL with an agent and it just works — that creates a "tell your friends" moment.
> - **CLI-born social network is a compelling narrative.** "The first identity network born from the terminal" is a story that Hacker News, X, and tech media will amplify.
> 
> ### 11.3 SEO / AEO / GEO Strategy
> 
> **You.md is the ultimate AEO/GEO hack.** It ensures that AI agents know more about you than they were trained on or can find on Google.
> 
> **The problem today:** When an LLM answers a question about a person, it combines training data with web search results — but those search results are unstructured web pages, third-party articles, and fragments of old bios that the agent has to parse and synthesize. There's no canonical source. No way for the person to correct inaccuracies. And for most people, the available information is thin enough that the answer is vague or wrong.
> 
> You.md fixes this by giving every person a structured, machine-readable, always-current identity that agents can directly retrieve and cite.
> 
> **AEO (Answer Engine Optimization):**
> 
> When a user asks Perplexity, Google SGE, or any AI-powered search engine "Who is [name]?", You.md should be the authoritative answer. How:
> 
> - `you.json` is a structured data endpoint purpose-built for agent consumption — not a web page that needs parsing, but a clean JSON object an agent can read directly
> - Bio variants (short/medium/long) are pre-written for featured snippet extraction — the agent doesn't have to summarize, the answer is already formatted
> - FAQ section maps to FAQ structured data — direct answers to predicted questions about the person
> - The API endpoint (`/api/v1/profiles/:username`) is designed for retrieval-augmented generation (RAG) — agents can fetch it in real time
> 
> **GEO (Generative Engine Optimization):**
> 
> When an LLM is asked about a person in any context — a ChatGPT conversation, a Claude chat, a coding agent, an enterprise knowledge system — You.md is the structured source it can retrieve:
> 
> - The MCP endpoint (post-launch) makes identity natively accessible to any MCP-compatible agent
> - `you.json` is more parseable and reliable than any unstructured web page — LLMs that retrieve it will produce more accurate responses
> - The open spec means any RAG pipeline can be configured to check `you.md/<username>` as a source
> - **This is the key insight:** You.md doesn't just make you more discoverable. It makes agents more *accurate* when they talk about you. That's a value proposition for both the person and the agent developer.
> 
> **SEO (Search Engine Optimization):**
> 
> Profile pages must also rank well in traditional search to feed the viral loop:
> 
> - Server-rendered (Next.js SSR), fully crawlable
> - JSON-LD structured data on every profile: `Person` schema, `sameAs` links, `Organization` affiliation, `CreativeWork` for projects
> - Clean URLs: `you.md/<username>`
> - Canonical meta tags, Open Graph tags, Twitter Cards
> - Page titles: `Houston Golden — Founder, BAMF Media | You.md`
> - Fast Core Web Vitals (critical for ranking)
> - Auto-generated Open Graph image (name + tagline + clean branding) — when shared, the link preview sells itself
> 
> **The pitch to users:** *"Claim your you.md. Give every AI agent on earth the context to know you, work with you, and represent you accurately — in seconds."*
> 
> ### 11.4 Profile Page as Viral Surface
> 
> The profile page must look premium out of the box, with zero customization required. Think **Notion meets Vercel** — structured, clean, authoritative.
> 
> **v1 profile page design philosophy:**
> - **Standardized layout.** Every profile uses the same structure. This ensures consistently high quality across all profiles and reinforces that You.md is infrastructure, not a page builder.
> - **Dark mode default.** Clean, minimal, monospace headings, tight spacing.
> - **Content-driven personalization.** Pages feel personal because of what's *in* them (your voice profile, your projects, your narrative), not because of visual customization. The pipeline's output is what makes each page unique.
> - **Featured projects with links** — prominent, above the fold. For founders with multiple ventures, this is the hero section.
> - **Auto-generated Open Graph card** — when shared on social, the link preview looks sharp (name, tagline, clean branding).
> - **JSON-LD structured data** — every page ships with Person schema, sameAs links, project data.
> - **"Powered by You.md — Claim yours" CTA** in footer — subtle, always present.
> 
> **What is NOT in v1:**
> - No custom themes, colors, or fonts
> - No drag-and-drop layout
> - No vibe-coded page customization
> - No embedded forms (newsletter subscribe is a future feature)
> - No media uploads or image galleries
> 
> **The standardization is a feature, not a limitation.** It guarantees that every you.md profile looks professional, loads fast, and ranks well. Custom profile theming may be explored post-launch (v1.2+) once the standardized design has proven its viral properties, but it is explicitly out of scope for initial months.
> 
> ## 13. Shareable Context Links
> 
> ### 13.1 The Problem
> 
> MCP endpoints and scoped API keys are the right long-term solution for agent-to-identity communication. But most real-world agent interactions today are simpler than that: you're in a ChatGPT conversation, or pasting context into a Cursor prompt, or talking to some new AI tool that has no MCP support. You just want to say *"here's who I am"* and paste a link.
> 
> ### 13.2 The Solution: Context Links
> 
> A **context link** is a URL with an embedded token that returns the user's identity bundle as plain text or JSON. The user generates it, controls what it exposes, sets an expiry, and pastes it wherever they need it.
> 
> ```
> https://you.md/ctx/houston/abc123def456
> ```
> 
> When an agent (or a user on behalf of an agent) fetches this URL, it returns the identity bundle — either the public `you.json` only, or the full bundle including private context, depending on the link's scope.
> 
> ### 13.3 How It Works
> 
> **Generating a context link:**
> 
> ```bash
> # CLI
> youmd link create                          # public context, 7-day expiry
> youmd link create --scope=full             # public + private context
> youmd link create --scope=full --ttl=24h   # expires in 24 hours
> youmd link create --scope=public --ttl=30d # public only, 30-day expiry
> 
> # Output:
> # Context link created:
> # https://you.md/ctx/houston/abc123def456
> # Scope: full (public + private)
> # Expires: 2026-03-17T12:00:00Z
> # Paste this into any AI conversation to share your context.
> ```
> 
> **Web UI:** Same flow. Button on dashboard: "Create context link" → choose scope → choose expiry → copy link.
> 
> **What the link returns:**
> 
> ```
> GET https://you.md/ctx/houston/abc123def456
> Accept: application/json
> 
> → 200 OK
> {
>   "schema": "you-md/v1",
>   "username": "houston",
>   "scope": "full",
>   "expires_at": "2026-03-17T12:00:00Z",
>   "identity": { ... },
>   "now": { ... },
>   "projects": [ ... ],
>   "preferences": { ... },
>   "analysis": { ... },
>   "private": { ... }       // only if scope=full
> }
> ```
> 
> If fetched as `text/plain` or `text/markdown` (or with no `Accept` header), returns the `you.md` entry file + private context as readable markdown. This is the "paste into ChatGPT" case — the user copies the URL, the agent fetches it (or the user fetches it and pastes the content), and the agent has full context.
> 
> ### 13.4 Link Properties
> 
> | Property | Options | Default |
> |---|---|---|
> | Scope | `public` (you.json only) / `full` (public + private) | `public` |
> | TTL (expiry) | 1h, 24h, 7d, 30d, 90d, never | 7d |
> | Max uses | 1, 10, 100, unlimited | unlimited |
> | Format | JSON, Markdown, or auto (via Accept header) | auto |
> 
> ### 13.5 Link Management
> 
> ```bash
> youmd link list              # show all active links
> youmd link revoke <id>       # immediately invalidate a link
> youmd link revoke --all      # revoke all links
> ```
> 
> ### 13.6 Why This Matters for Launch
> 
> Context links solve the "how do I actually use this?" problem on day one. The launch flow becomes:
> 
> 1. Create your you.md (via skill + CLI or web)
> 2. Get your public profile at `you.md/<username>`
> 3. Generate a context link
> 4. Paste it into any AI conversation: *"Here's my context: https://you.md/ctx/houston/abc123"*
> 5. The agent reads it and now knows who you are
> 
> This works with **every agent that can fetch a URL** — which is nearly all of them. No MCP. No API key setup. No integration needed. Just a link.
> 
> It's also the bridge to the AEO/GEO value prop: the same link you paste into ChatGPT is the same structured data that Perplexity can retrieve when someone asks about you. One artifact, two use cases.
> 
> ### 13.7 Data Model Addition
> 
> ```typescript
> // Add to convex/schema.ts
> contextLinks: defineTable({
>   userId: v.id("users"),
>   token: v.string(),              // random URL-safe token
>   scope: v.union(v.literal("public"), v.literal("full")),
>   expiresAt: v.optional(v.number()),   // timestamp, null = never
>   maxUses: v.optional(v.number()),     // null = unlimited
>   useCount: v.number(),
>   revokedAt: v.optional(v.number()),
>   createdAt: v.number(),
> })
>   .index("by_token", ["token"])
>   .index("by_userId", ["userId"]),
> ```
> 
> ### 13.8 Security Considerations
> 
> - Tokens are 32-byte random values, URL-safe encoded
> - Full-scope links expose private vault content — the UI and CLI must warn users before creating them
> - Links with `full` scope require the user to be on Pro plan (private vault is a Pro feature)
> - All link fetches are logged in `profileViews` with `isContextLink: true`
> - Revocation is instant — fetching a revoked link returns 401
> - Links do NOT expose raw source data or analysis artifacts — only the compiled identity bundle + private context
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 12.1 Thesis
> 
> One agent framework reading `you.json` as a context source validates the entire protocol. One integration is worth more than a thousand profile signups at this stage.
> 
> ### 12.2 Strategy: Bottom-Up Framework Adoption
> 
> The goal is to get agent frameworks to natively support `you.json` as a context input, the same way they already support `agent.md` or `CLAUDE.md`.
> 
> **Approach:**
> 1. Start with small, accessible open-source frameworks where a single PR can add support
> 2. Build up a list of "You.md compatible" tools
> 3. Use that momentum to approach larger frameworks
> 4. Eventually, "reads you.json" becomes a standard capability expectation
> 
> ### 12.3 Target Frameworks (Prioritized)
> 
> **Tier 1 — Small / high-access (Months 1–2)**
> Target: Frameworks where a single contributor PR can add You.md support. These are credibility-building.
> 
> | Framework | Why | Action |
> |---|---|---|
> | OpenClaw forks (OpenFang, TinyClaw, etc.) | Small communities, eager for differentiation, founder likely reachable | PR: add `--you-md <url>` flag or `you.json` auto-detection in project root |
> | Aider | Popular open-source coding agent, active contributor community | PR: read `you.json` from project root or `~/.youmd/` for user context |
> | Goose (Block) | Open-source agent, growing community | PR: add You.md as a context provider |
> | GPT-Engineer / Smol Developer | Simple agent architectures, easy to extend | PR: inject `you.json` into system prompt |
> | CrewAI | Multi-agent framework, "human context" is a natural fit | PR: add `you.json` as a crew member context source |
> 
> **Tier 2 — Medium / established (Months 2–4)**
> Target: Frameworks with more process but where You.md support makes obvious sense.
> 
> | Framework | Why | Action |
> |---|---|---|
> | OpenClaw (main) | Large community, defines patterns others follow | PR or proposal: native `you.md` context support |
> | LangChain / LangGraph | Massive ecosystem, adding a "human context" loader is natural | Contribute a `YouMdLoader` document loader |
> | AutoGen (Microsoft) | Multi-agent, human-in-the-loop is core to their model | Proposal: `you.json` as human participant context |
> | Semantic Kernel (Microsoft) | Enterprise-oriented, structured context is valued | Plugin: You.md context provider |
> 
> **Tier 3 — Large / aspirational (Months 4–6+)**
> Target: Platform-level integrations that signal mainstream adoption.
> 
> | Platform | Why | Action |
> |---|---|---|
> | Claude Code (Anthropic) | If Claude Code reads `you.json`, that's instant legitimacy | Propose via Anthropic developer relations |
> | Cursor | Millions of users, already reads `.cursorrules` | Propose `you.json` as user-level context (not project-level) |
> | Windsurf / Codex CLI | Growing agent-native editors | Integration proposals |
> | Vercel AI SDK | If the SDK has a You.md provider, every app built on it can consume identity | Contribute a provider package |
> 
> ### 12.4 The PR Template
> 
> For Tier 1 and 2 frameworks, the contribution should be:
> 1. A single file/module that reads `you.json` from a known location (`./you.json`, `~/.youmd/you.json`, or a URL)
> 2. Injects relevant context into the agent's system prompt or context window
> 3. Respects public/private boundaries from the manifest
> 4. Links back to the You.md spec
> 
> This should be a 50–200 line PR. Keep it small. Make it easy to merge.
> 
> ### 12.5 "Compatible with You.md" Badge
> 
> Post-launch, create a simple badge/shield that frameworks can add to their README:
> 
> ```markdown
> [![Compatible with You.md](https://you.md/badge.svg)](https://you.md)
> ```
> 
> This creates visible social proof in the agent ecosystem.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Appendix A: Onboarding Agent Personality
> 
> The agent that guides users through onboarding (CLI and web) has a defined personality:
> 
> - Direct but warm. Not corporate. Not quirky.
> - Calm confidence. Knows what it's doing.
> - Subtle dry humor when appropriate.
> - Never cringe. Never over-familiar. Never uses emoji.
> - CLI-native tone — reads like well-written terminal output.
> 
> Examples:
> ```
> "Cool. Drop your website and I'll go read it."
> "Found 14 links on your site. 3 look like keepers. Want to review?"
> "LinkedIn scraped. You've had 6 jobs. Impressive, or chaotic. Let's find out."
> "Your public presence tells me you're a growth marketing founder who writes about AI. Sound right?"
> ```
> 
> This personality is a guideline for prompt engineering, not a system to build.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Appendix B: Open Questions
> 
> These are unresolved decisions that need to be made during Milestone 0–1.
> 
> 1. **Clerk configuration:** Which Clerk plan? Do we need Clerk Organizations for future team bundles, or is that premature?
> 2. **Scraping reliability:** Apify's LinkedIn scraper may break. What's the fallback? Manual paste? Browser extension? Needs a degradation plan.
> 3. **LLM model selection:** Which model for extraction vs. analysis? Cost vs. quality trade-off. Likely: fast model (Haiku-tier) for extraction, strong model (Sonnet-tier) for analysis and voice profiling.
> 4. **Username policy:** Min/max length, allowed characters, reserved words list. Define before Milestone 0.
> 5. **Spec governance:** Who can propose changes to `you-md/v1`? RFC process? Or benevolent dictator for now?
> 6. **Private vault UX:** How does the user see their private data if it's encrypted? Decrypt on read in the browser? Or only via CLI/API?
> 7. **Skill format validation:** skills.sh and clawhub.ai may have different format requirements. Validate before Milestone 4.
> 8. **Convex limits:** Validate that Convex file storage and document size limits work for large bundles (20+ sources). Stress-test early.
> 9. **YouTube transcript extraction:** Apify's YouTube scraper can pull channel data, but transcript extraction reliability varies. Evaluate dedicated transcript APIs (e.g., Superpowered, AssemblyAI) as a supplement.
> 10. **Tier 1 framework selection:** Finalize which 5 frameworks to target first. Prioritize by: maintainer accessibility, community size, ease of PR, and alignment with You.md's target user.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Appendix C: Decision Log
> 
> | Date | Decision | Rationale |
> |---|---|---|
> | 2026-03-02 | Directory-based bundle, not single file | Identity is too complex for one file. Agents need navigable structure. |
> | 2026-03-02 | OpenRouter for LLM routing | Avoids vendor lock-in. Cost optimization across models. |
> | 2026-03-02 | CLI-first distribution | Developer credibility. Protocol products are adopted bottom-up. |
> | 2026-03-02 | Dual CLI install: curl + npx | `curl` is platform-agnostic, no runtime dependency. `npx create-youmd` is smoother for Node.js users. Both converge on same binary. |
> | 2026-03-02 | Web onboarding as secondary path | Same pipeline, visual UI. Exists for non-terminal users. CLI is the default and the primary onboarding. |
> | 2026-03-02 | Skill as primary discovery channel | Lower friction than asking devs to install a new CLI cold. Skill is the front door, CLI is the engine. |
> | 2026-03-02 | Infrastructure positioning, not consumer | "Identity file for the agent internet" — not "cool profile page." Consumer layer emerges from usage. |
> | 2026-03-02 | No social features in v1 | No followers, feeds, DMs. Identity network layer is a future possibility, not a v1 feature. |
> | 2026-03-02 | Standardized profile design, no customization in v1 | Consistency ensures quality. Notion-meets-Vercel aesthetic. Theming is v1.2+ at earliest. |
> | 2026-03-02 | Markdown for humans, JSON for machines | Best of both worlds. Humans don't want to edit JSON. Machines don't want to parse markdown. |
> | 2026-03-02 | Milestone-based scope with hard boundaries | Prevents scope creep. Each milestone is shippable independently. |
> | 2026-03-02 | Convex over PostgreSQL | Reactive queries, built-in job queue, file storage, TypeScript-native. Fewer moving parts. |
> | 2026-03-02 | Adapt BAMF Media voice profiling system | Years of production-tested prompt chains for author voice analysis. Not building from scratch. |
> | 2026-03-02 | Bottom-up framework integration as primary growth | Protocols win by being in the dependency tree, not by marketing. PR to frameworks > ad spend. |
> | 2026-03-02 | Launch angle: "Onboard any AI in seconds" + AEO/GEO | Lead with instant agent onboarding (demo-able, tangible). AEO/GEO is the deeper value prop that follows. Not defensive ("control") — expansive ("onboard, know, work with, represent"). |
> | 2026-03-02 | Context links as primary sharing mechanism | Works with any agent that can fetch a URL. No MCP, no API key setup. Lowest possible friction. Bridge to AEO/GEO. |
> | 2026-03-02 | Dual positioning: for your agents + for everyone else's agents | Not just a personal context tool. Also the canonical source agents retrieve when asked *about* you. AEO/GEO is a core value prop, not a feature. |
> | 2026-03-02 | Verified badges (person + business) at v1.1 | Critical for AEO/GEO thesis. Agents need a trust signal. Reserve `verification` field in v1 schema. |
> | 2026-03-02 | SEO/AEO/GEO as core feature | Profile pages must improve discoverability in search engines and LLMs. Part of the value prop, not an afterthought. |
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Appendix D: Glossary
> 
> | Term | Definition |
> |---|---|
> | **Bundle** | A complete You.md identity — the directory of files (you.md, you.json, manifest.json, etc.) |
> | **Manifest** | `manifest.json` — the index that tells agents what's in the bundle and what they can access |
> | **Ingestion** | The pipeline that scrapes, extracts, and analyzes a source URL |
> | **Compilation** | The step that generates `you.json` and `you.md` from profile data + analysis |
> | **Private vault** | Encrypted storage for context the user wants agents to have but not the public |
> | **Scoped key** | An API key with specific permissions (e.g., `read:public` only) |
> | **Source** | An external URL (website, LinkedIn, etc.) that feeds the ingestion pipeline |
> | **Artifact** | A generated analysis file (voice profile, topic map, bio variants, etc.) |

**2026-03-17 17:11:25 UTC**
> # PRD: You.md
> 
> **Identity as Code**
> 
> Founder: Houston Golden
> Package: `youmd`
> Status: Pre-Build
> Last Updated: 2026-03-02
> PRD Version: 2.0
> 
> ## 15. Visual & Brand System
> 
> ### 15.1 Brand Concept
> 
> **Visual metaphor: Ascension.**
> 
> A human figure being drawn upward into a ring of light — identity captured, structured, and shared with a higher intelligence. This is the core brand image. It communicates:
> 
> - Your identity is *elevated*, not just stored
> - There's something almost spiritual about making yourself legible to AI — it's a new kind of self-knowledge
> - The process is warm and human, not cold and technical
> - You're choosing to share yourself, not being surveilled
> 
> The tone is: **optimistic sci-fi meets calm confidence.** Think Arrival, not Terminator. The imagery says "first contact" — a human meeting a higher intelligence halfway, on their own terms.
> 
> ### 15.2 Color System
> 
> Derived from the hero gradient — warm human tones at the base, ascending into cool ethereal tones:
> 
> | Token | Value | Usage |
> |---|---|---|
> | `--coral` | `#E8857A` | Warm accent, CTAs, human-side elements |
> | `--blush` | `#F0A898` | Secondary warm, hover states, soft highlights |
> | `--sky` | `#7ABED0` | Primary brand blue, mid-gradient, links |
> | `--ether` | `#B8D8E8` | Light UI surfaces, card backgrounds |
> | `--gold` | `#F4D78C` | Premium accent, Pro features, verified badges, light source |
> | `--light` | `#FFF8E7` | Ethereal glow, highlights, focal points |
> | `--void` | `#0A0E1A` | Deep background, text on light surfaces |
> | `--ink` | `#1A1F2E` | Secondary dark, card backgrounds in dark mode |
> | `--mist` | `#8899AA` | Muted text, secondary labels, borders |
> 
> **The gradient direction matters:** warm (coral, blush) at the bottom → cool (sky, ether) in the middle → luminous (gold, light) at the top. This mirrors the hero image and the product metaphor: grounded human identity ascending toward agent intelligence.
> 
> **Dark mode is default** — the product lives in the sky/void space. Light mode inverts but preserves the warmth.
> 
> ### 15.3 Typography
> 
> | Element | Font | Weight | Notes |
> |---|---|---|---|
> | Logo / brand mark | Monospace (e.g., `JetBrains Mono`, `Berkeley Mono`) | Regular | `you.md` always rendered in monospace — it's a filename |
> | Headings | System sans-serif (`Inter`, `-apple-system` stack) | 500–600 | Clean, not decorative |
> | Body | System sans-serif | 400 | Readable, tight line-height |
> | Code / CLI references | Monospace | 400 | Inline code, terminal output, file paths |
> | Taglines / hero copy | System sans-serif | 300–400 | Light weight for the ethereal feel |
> 
> **The monospace logo is non-negotiable.** `you.md` is a filename. It should always look like one. This reinforces the "identity as code" positioning every time someone sees the brand.
> 
> ### 15.4 Design Principles
> 
> 1. **Warm, not cold.** AI products default to blue-steel-clinical. You.md is warm. Coral tones, soft gradients, golden light. The message: this is about *you*, the human.
> 
> 2. **Spacious, not dense.** Generous whitespace. The profile page should breathe. The hero should feel vast. Tightness is for the CLI output, not the brand.
> 
> 3. **Ethereal, not flashy.** Subtle glows, soft gradients, gentle animations. No hard neon. No aggressive motion. The visual language says "calm intelligence," not "startup energy."
> 
> 4. **Monospace anchors the tech.** Every time `you.md`, a CLI command, a file path, or a code reference appears, it's in monospace. This is the visual thread that connects the warm brand to the technical product.
> 
> 5. **The beam of light is the recurring motif.** The hero's column of light — representing identity being structured and elevated — should echo throughout the product: as a loading state, as a subtle glow behind profile photos, as the line that connects elements on the profile page.
> 
> ### 15.5 Profile Page Design
> 
> The public profile page at `you.md/<username>` follows the brand system:
> 
> - **Dark background** (`--void` or `--ink`) — the profile lives in the sky
> - **Warm accents** for the user's name, project links, CTAs (`--coral`, `--gold`)
> - **Cool tones** for structure and secondary text (`--sky`, `--mist`)
> - **Subtle vertical glow** behind the user's identity section — echoing the beam of light
> - **Monospace** for the username, file references, and the "you.md/username" URL
> - **No profile photos in v1** — the identity is text and structure, not a headshot (revisit later)
> - **Standardized layout** — every profile has the same structure, differentiated by content not design
> - **"Powered by You.md" footer** uses the brand gradient subtly
> 
> ### 15.6 CLI Visual Identity
> 
> The CLI reflects the brand within terminal constraints:
> 
> - **Minimal color use** — only use ANSI colors when they communicate meaning (green for success, yellow for warnings, cyan for links/URLs)
> - **The `you.md` wordmark** appears once at the top of `create-youmd` output
> - **Progress indicators** use a simple vertical pipeline aesthetic (├── , └──) — echoing the beam/column motif
> - **No emoji. No spinners. No skeleton blocks.**
> - **Subtle text shimmer or pixel grid loader** allowed for build steps (optional, not required)
> 
> ### 15.7 Open Graph / Social Cards
> 
> Auto-generated for every profile. When someone shares `you.md/houston` on X, LinkedIn, or Slack:
> 
> - **Background:** gradient from `--ink` at bottom to `--void` at top, with a subtle `--gold` glow at center
> - **Content:** Username in monospace, display name, tagline, `you.md` brand mark
> - **Feel:** looks like a terminal output card floating in the sky
> - **Dimensions:** 1200×630 (standard OG)
> 
> Generated server-side (via Vercel OG or Satori). No manual design per profile.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 0. How to Read This Document
> 
> This PRD is the canonical build spec for You.md. It is written for the engineering team.
> 
> - **Sections 1–2** define what we're building and why, in plain language.
> - **Section 3** defines the open spec — the data format that everything else depends on.
> - **Section 4** defines the technical architecture — infrastructure, services, data flow.
> - **Section 5** defines the product surface — CLI, web, API — and exactly what ships in v1.
> - **Section 6** defines phased milestones with hard scope boundaries.
> - **Section 7** covers security, privacy, and trust.
> - **Section 8** covers go-to-market, monetization, and success criteria.
> - **Appendices** include glossary, open questions, and decision log.
> 
> If something isn't in Section 6's milestone scope, we don't build it yet.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 1. Problem
> 
> AI agents are becoming the primary interface between humans and software. But agents have no reliable way to understand who they're working for — or who they're talking *about*.
> 
> **The agent context problem (personal):**
> 
> Every time you use a new AI tool, you restate your tone, re-explain your role, rebuild memory from scratch. Your identity is fragmented across dozens of systems, none of which talk to each other.
> 
> **The agent knowledge problem (public):**
> 
> When someone asks an AI agent about you — who you are, what you do, what you've built — the agent pieces together an answer from training data and web search results. Even with search, the results are unstructured web pages the agent has to parse and guess from. The information is often incomplete, outdated, or just wrong — and you have zero control over what it says.
> 
> Google solved this for search with Knowledge Panels and structured data. **Nobody has solved it for agents.**
> 
> Today, if an LLM is asked "Who is [your name]?", the answer depends on whatever the model finds — scraped web pages, third-party articles, fragments of old bios. For most people, the answer is thin or nonexistent. For well-known people, it's a patchwork of unverified sources that may contradict each other. For everyone, there's no canonical source the agent can trust, and no way for the person to correct what's wrong.
> 
> You.md solves both problems with a single artifact: a structured, portable identity bundle that agents can consume directly — authoritative, current, and controlled by the person it represents.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 2. Solution
> 
> **You.md is the identity file for the agent internet.**
> 
> The agent ecosystem is converging on markdown-based config files for identity and instructions: `CLAUDE.md`, `.cursorrules`, `agent.md`, `soul.md`. These all give agents their identity. What's conspicuously missing is the human side of that handshake. You.md completes the protocol. Agent has a spec. Human has a spec. They negotiate context.
> 
> It consists of:
> 
> 1. **An open file spec** (`you-md/v1`) — a directory-based identity format that anyone can implement, self-host, or extend.
> 2. **A hosted platform** (`you.md/<username>`) — a registry, editor, encrypted vault, and API layer that makes the spec immediately useful.
> 3. **A CLI** (`youmd`) — a terminal-native tool for generating, building, and publishing identity bundles.
> 4. **An agent skill** — a packaged instruction set that teaches coding agents (Claude Code, OpenClaw, Codex CLI) how to use You.md, serving as the primary discovery and onboarding channel.
> 5. **An agent onboarding pipeline** — a system that uses Perplexity Sonar for discovery, Apify for structured platform scraping, Firecrawl for web content, and LLMs via OpenRouter for extraction and analysis. Turns a few URLs into a complete identity bundle.
> 
> The open spec creates legitimacy and ecosystem potential. The hosted platform creates adoption and revenue. The CLI creates developer credibility. The skill creates frictionless discovery.
> 
> ### 2.1 Positioning (Canonical)
> 
> **Launch headline:** *"Your identity file for the agent internet. Onboard any AI in seconds."*
> 
> **Supporting lines (pick per context):**
> - *"Give every agent full context — as if it's been working with you for years."*
> - *"Written in the native language of agents. Readable by any LLM on earth."*
> - *"The agent internet has soul.md and agent.md. Now humans have you.md."*
> 
> **The core framing:**
> 
> You.md is agent-native identity. It's not a human profile that agents happen to read — it's a structured identity bundle *written in the format agents already understand*: markdown files, JSON schemas, API endpoints. When an agent reads your you.md, it doesn't need to parse a web page or guess from training data. It gets structured, authoritative, current context about who you are, how you work, how you communicate, and what you're building.
> 
> **The value prop:**
> 
> 1. **Onboard any agent instantly.** Share your you.md with Claude, ChatGPT, Cursor, or any AI tool — via URL, context link, MCP, or API — and it has full context in seconds. No more re-explaining yourself. No more rebuilding memory. Every new tool starts where the last one left off. *This is the primary value prop. Immediate, tangible, demo-able.*
> 
> 2. **Be known accurately across the agent internet (AEO/GEO).** When someone asks any AI about you, You.md is the structured, authoritative source it can retrieve and cite — not a patchwork of scraped web pages and unverified third-party content. Your Google Knowledge Panel for the agent era — always current, always accurate, always under your control. *This is a powerful secondary angle, especially for founders and public figures, but not the launch focus.*
> 
> 3. **Manage your identity from the terminal.** Your you.md lives as local files, managed via CLI (`youmd`), driven by your coding agent (Claude Code, OpenClaw, Codex CLI), and published to `you.md/<username>`. Update your identity the same way you push code. *Developer credibility.*
> 
> **Why it works:**
> 
> Your you.md is written in `.md` — the native format of agent instructions. It uses JSON schemas that any LLM can parse without transformation. It's served via API endpoints designed for retrieval-augmented generation. And it auto-updates across platforms — change it once in your terminal, and every agent that reads it gets the current version.
> 
> **The pitch in one breath:** *"You.md is your identity file for the agent internet. Claim your username, build your profile from the CLI, and instantly give every AI agent on earth the context to know you, work with you, and represent you accurately."*
> 
> Launch as pure infrastructure. Let the consumer layer emerge from usage.
> 
> ### 2.2 The `you.md` / `soul.md` / `agent.md` Symmetry
> 
> This is the deeper thesis and the strategic framing for protocol adoption:
> 
> | File | Represents | Purpose |
> |---|---|---|
> | `agent.md` / `CLAUDE.md` / `.cursorrules` | The agent's instructions | Tells the agent how to behave in a project |
> | `soul.md` | The agent's identity/persona | Gives the agent a personality, values, voice |
> | **`you.md`** | **The human's identity** | **Gives agents structured context about the human they're working for** |
> 
> These three files form a complete context handshake:
> - The agent knows who it is (`soul.md`)
> - The agent knows how to behave (`agent.md`)
> - The agent knows who it's working for (`you.md`)
> 
> You.md is the missing piece. This symmetry is core to the protocol positioning and should be emphasized in all external communications.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 3. Open Spec: `you-md/v1`
> 
> This section is the most important in the document. Everything else — the CLI, the web UI, the API — is a consumer of this spec. If the spec is wrong, everything downstream breaks.
> 
> ### 3.1 Design Principles
> 
> - **Directory-based, not single-file.** An identity is a bundle of related files, not a monolith.
> - **Markdown-first for humans, JSON for machines.** Humans author in `.md`. The system compiles to `.json`.
> - **Explicit public/private boundaries.** Every file is either public or private. There is no ambiguity.
> - **Manifest-routed.** Agents read `manifest.json` first. It tells them what exists, what's accessible, and where to find it.
> - **Extensible within versioning rules.** Users can add custom directories. The spec defines required primitives and reserved paths.
> 
> ### 3.2 Required Primitives
> 
> Every valid `you-md/v1` bundle MUST contain:
> 
> | File | Type | Purpose |
> |---|---|---|
> | `you.md` | Markdown | Human-readable identity entry point. The "front page." |
> | `you.json` | JSON | Compiled machine-readable output. Generated, not hand-edited. |
> | `manifest.json` | JSON | Directory map, permission declarations, schema version, source registry. |
> 
> These three files are non-negotiable. A bundle without all three is invalid.
> 
> ### 3.3 Directory Structure
> 
> ```
> you/
> ├── you.md                    # REQUIRED — human-readable entry file
> ├── you.json                  # REQUIRED — compiled machine-readable output
> ├── manifest.json             # REQUIRED — directory map + permissions
> │
> ├── profile/                  # User-authored identity content
> │   ├── about.md              # Bio, background, identity narrative
> │   ├── now.md                # Current focus (inspired by nownownow.com)
> │   ├── projects.md           # Active projects with status
> │   ├── values.md             # Core values, beliefs, non-negotiables
> │   └── links.md              # Annotated links (website, social, etc.)
> │
> ├── preferences/              # Agent-facing configuration
> │   ├── agent.md              # How agents should behave when representing this person
> │   ├── writing.md            # Tone, voice, style preferences
> │   └── formatting.md         # Output formatting rules
> │
> ├── sources/                  # Raw ingested data (generated by pipeline)
> │   ├── website/
> │   │   ├── raw.html
> │   │   └── extracted.json
> │   ├── linkedin/
> │   │   ├── raw.json
> │   │   └── extracted.json
> │   ├── x/
> │   │   ├── raw.json
> │   │   └── extracted.json
> │   └── blog/
> │       ├── raw.html
> │       └── extracted.json
> │
> ├── analysis/                 # LLM-derived artifacts (generated by pipeline)
> │   ├── author_voice.md       # Writing style analysis
> │   ├── topic_map.json        # Structured topic/expertise graph
> │   ├── bio_variants.md       # Multiple bio lengths (1-line, 3-line, paragraph)
> │   ├── narrative_arcs.md     # Career/life story threads
> │   └── faq.md                # Predicted questions about this person
> │
> └── private/                  # Encrypted context (never served publicly)
>     ├── private.md
>     └── private.json
> ```
> 
> **Reserved paths:** `profile/`, `preferences/`, `sources/`, `analysis/`, `private/` are reserved by the spec. Users may add custom top-level directories (e.g., `portfolio/`, `research/`), which will be listed in the manifest under `custom_paths`.
> 
> ### 3.4 Manifest Schema
> 
> ```jsonc
> {
>   "schema": "you-md/v1",
>   "username": "houston",
>   "generated_at": "2026-03-02T12:00:00Z",
>   "compiler_version": "0.1.0",
> 
>   "paths": {
>     "public": [
>       "you.md",
>       "you.json",
>       "profile/about.md",
>       "profile/now.md",
>       "profile/projects.md",
>       "profile/values.md",
>       "profile/links.md",
>       "preferences/agent.md",
>       "preferences/writing.md",
>       "preferences/formatting.md",
>       "analysis/author_voice.md",
>       "analysis/topic_map.json",
>       "analysis/bio_variants.md",
>       "analysis/narrative_arcs.md",
>       "analysis/faq.md"
>     ],
>     "private": [
>       "private/private.md",
>       "private/private.json"
>     ],
>     "scoped": []
>   },
> 
>   "sources": {
>     "website": {
>       "url": "https://houstongolden.com",
>       "last_fetched": "2026-03-01T08:00:00Z",
>       "status": "active"
>     },
>     "linkedin": {
>       "url": "https://linkedin.com/in/houstongolden",
>       "last_fetched": "2026-03-01T08:00:00Z",
>       "status": "active"
>     }
>   },
> 
>   "update_policy": {
>     "auto_refresh": false,
>     "refresh_interval_days": null,
>     "require_approval": true
>   },
> 
>   "custom_paths": []
> }
> ```
> 
> ### 3.5 `you.json` Compiled Output Schema
> 
> This is what agents consume. It is generated by the build step, never hand-edited.
> 
> ```jsonc
> {
>   "schema": "you-md/v1",
>   "username": "houston",
>   "generated_at": "2026-03-02T12:00:00Z",
> 
>   "identity": {
>     "name": "Houston Golden",
>     "tagline": "Founder, BAMF Media. Building You.md.",
>     "location": "Miami, FL",
>     "bio": {
>       "short": "...",       // 1 line
>       "medium": "...",      // 3 lines
>       "long": "..."         // full paragraph
>     }
>   },
> 
>   "now": {
>     "focus": ["Building You.md", "Scaling BAMF Media"],
>     "updated_at": "2026-03-01"
>   },
> 
>   "projects": [
>     {
>       "name": "You.md",
>       "role": "Founder",
>       "status": "building",
>       "url": "https://you.md",
>       "description": "Identity as code for the agent internet."
>     }
>   ],
> 
>   "values": ["Build in public", "Extreme ownership", "Ship fast"],
> 
>   "links": {
>     "website": "https://houstongolden.com",
>     "linkedin": "https://linkedin.com/in/houstongolden",
>     "x": "https://x.com/houstongolden"
>   },
> 
>   "preferences": {
>     "agent": {
>       "tone": "direct, confident, no fluff",
>       "formality": "casual-professional",
>       "avoid": ["corporate jargon", "passive voice"]
>     },
>     "writing": {
>       "style": "short paragraphs, punchy sentences",
>       "format": "markdown preferred"
>     }
>   },
> 
>   "analysis": {
>     "topics": ["growth marketing", "AI agents", "identity protocols"],
>     "voice_summary": "Direct, high-energy, founder-coded.",
>     "credibility_signals": [
>       "Founded BAMF Media (8-figure agency)",
>       "LinkedIn growth pioneer"
>     ]
>   },
> 
>   "meta": {
>     "sources_used": ["website", "linkedin", "x"],
>     "last_updated": "2026-03-02T12:00:00Z",
>     "compiler_version": "0.1.0"
>   },
> 
>   "verification": null
>   // Reserved for v1.1. When populated:
>   // {
>   //   "status": "verified" | "unverified",
>   //   "type": "person" | "business",
>   //   "methods": ["domain", "linkedin", "github"],
>   //   "verified_at": "2026-05-01T00:00:00Z"
>   // }
> }
> ```
> 
> ### 3.6 `you.md` Entry File Format
> 
> ```markdown
> ---
> schema: you-md/v1
> name: Houston Golden
> username: houston
> generated_at: 2026-03-02
> ---
> 
> # Houston Golden
> 
> Founder, BAMF Media. Building You.md.
> 
> ## Now
> 
> - Building You.md — identity as code for the agent internet
> - Scaling BAMF Media
> 
> ## Projects
> 
> - **You.md** — identity file standard + hosted platform (Founder, building)
> - **BAMF Media** — growth marketing agency (Founder/CEO, active)
> 
> ## Values
> 
> - Build in public
> - Extreme ownership
> - Ship fast
> 
> ## Agent Preferences
> 
> Tone: direct, confident, no fluff.
> Avoid: corporate jargon, passive voice.
> Format: short paragraphs, punchy sentences.
> 
> ## Links
> 
> - Website: https://houstongolden.com
> - LinkedIn: https://linkedin.com/in/houstongolden
> - X: https://x.com/houstongolden
> 
> ---
> 
> > Full context: see manifest.json
> ```
> 
> ### 3.7 Spec Versioning Rules
> 
> - The spec version is `you-md/v1`. All files in a bundle must declare the same version.
> - Minor additions (new optional fields) are backward-compatible within `v1`.
> - Breaking changes (removed required fields, restructured paths) require `v2`.
> - The spec will be published at `spec.you.md` and versioned in a public GitHub repo.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 4. Technical Architecture
> 
> ### 4.1 System Overview
> 
> ```
> ┌─────────────┐     ┌──────────────┐     ┌──────────────────┐
> │   CLI        │────▶│  API Server   │────▶│  Database         │
> │  (youmd)     │     │  (REST)       │     │  (Postgres)       │
> └─────────────┘     └──────┬───────┘     └──────────────────┘
>                            │
> ┌─────────────┐            │              ┌──────────────────┐
> │   Web UI     │───────────┘              │  Object Storage   │
> │  (Next.js)   │                          │  (S3/R2)          │
> └─────────────┘                           └──────────────────┘
>                                                     ▲
>                     ┌──────────────┐                 │
>                     │  Ingestion    │────────────────┘
>                     │  Pipeline     │
>                     └──────┬───────┘
>                            │
>               ┌────────────┼────────────┐
>               ▼            ▼            ▼
>         ┌──────────┐ ┌──────────┐ ┌──────────┐
>         │ Perplexity│ │  Apify   │ │ Firecrawl│
>         │ (Search)  │ │ (Scrape) │ │ (Scrape) │
>         └──────────┘ └──────────┘ └──────────┘
>               │            │            │
>               ▼            ▼            ▼
>         ┌──────────────────────────────────┐
>         │   LLM Layer (via OpenRouter)      │
>         │   - Extraction                    │
>         │   - Analysis                      │
>         │   - Compilation                   │
>         └──────────────────────────────────┘
> ```
> 
> ### 4.2 Tech Stack
> 
> | Layer | Technology | Rationale |
> |---|---|---|
> | **Backend + Database** | Convex | Reactive, serverless, real-time, TypeScript-native. Replaces separate API server + DB + queue. Convex functions serve as the API layer, database, and job scheduler. |
> | **Web Frontend** | Next.js 14+ (App Router) | SSR for profile pages (SEO critical), React for editor/dashboard |
> | **File Storage** | Convex File Storage | Bundle artifacts, source files. Native to Convex. |
> | **Auth** | Clerk (via Convex integration) | Username claim, session management. Convex has first-class Clerk support. |
> | **CLI** | TypeScript, published to npm as `youmd` | |
> | **LLM Routing** | OpenRouter | Multi-model, cost-optimized, single API |
> | **Search** | Perplexity Sonar API | Discovery + web search |
> | **Scraping** | Apify (LinkedIn, X), Firecrawl (general web) | Structured scraping at scale |
> | **Encryption** | AES-256-GCM | Private vault encryption at rest |
> | **Hosting** | Vercel (web) | Convex handles backend hosting natively |
> | **Job Queue** | Convex scheduled functions + actions | Replaces BullMQ/Redis. Native async job execution. |
> 
> ### 4.3 Data Model (Convex)
> 
> Convex uses a document-based model with TypeScript schema definitions. All queries are reactive by default.
> 
> ```typescript
> // convex/schema.ts
> import { defineSchema, defineTable } from "convex/server";
> import { v } from "convex/values";
> 
> export default defineSchema({
>   users: defineTable({
>     clerkId: v.string(),
>     username: v.string(),
>     email: v.string(),
>     displayName: v.optional(v.string()),
>     plan: v.union(v.literal("free"), v.literal("pro")),
>   })
>     .index("by_username", ["username"])
>     .index("by_clerkId", ["clerkId"])
>     .index("by_email", ["email"]),
> 
>   bundles: defineTable({
>     userId: v.id("users"),
>     version: v.number(),
>     schemaVersion: v.string(),         // "you-md/v1"
>     manifest: v.any(),                  // manifest.json content
>     youJson: v.any(),                   // compiled you.json
>     youMd: v.string(),                  // you.md content
>     pageTemplate: v.optional(v.string()), // custom profile page template (v1.1+)
>     isPublished: v.boolean(),
>   })
>     .index("by_userId", ["userId"])
>     .index("by_userId_version", ["userId", "version"]),
> 
>   sources: defineTable({
>     userId: v.id("users"),
>     sourceType: v.string(),            // "website" | "linkedin" | "x" | "blog"
>     sourceUrl: v.string(),
>     rawStorageId: v.optional(v.id("_storage")),  // Convex file storage ref
>     extracted: v.optional(v.any()),     // structured extraction
>     status: v.union(
>       v.literal("pending"),
>       v.literal("fetching"),
>       v.literal("fetched"),
>       v.literal("extracting"),
>       v.literal("extracted"),
>       v.literal("failed")
>     ),
>     lastFetched: v.optional(v.number()),  // timestamp
>     errorMessage: v.optional(v.string()),
>   })
>     .index("by_userId", ["userId"])
>     .index("by_userId_type", ["userId", "sourceType"]),
> 
>   analysisArtifacts: defineTable({
>     userId: v.id("users"),
>     artifactType: v.string(),          // "author_voice" | "topic_map" | "bio_variants" | etc.
>     content: v.any(),
>   })
>     .index("by_userId", ["userId"])
>     .index("by_userId_type", ["userId", "artifactType"]),
> 
>   apiKeys: defineTable({
>     userId: v.id("users"),
>     keyHash: v.string(),                // SHA-256 hash of the key
>     label: v.optional(v.string()),
>     scopes: v.array(v.string()),       // ["read:public", "read:private", "write:bundle"]
>     lastUsedAt: v.optional(v.number()),
>     revokedAt: v.optional(v.number()),
>   })
>     .index("by_userId", ["userId"])
>     .index("by_keyHash", ["keyHash"]),
> 
>   privateVault: defineTable({
>     userId: v.id("users"),
>     encryptedMd: v.bytes(),             // AES-256-GCM encrypted
>     encryptedJson: v.bytes(),
>     iv: v.bytes(),
>   })
>     .index("by_userId", ["userId"]),
> 
>   // Pipeline job tracking
>   pipelineJobs: defineTable({
>     userId: v.id("users"),
>     sourceId: v.optional(v.id("sources")),
>     stage: v.union(
>       v.literal("discover"),
>       v.literal("fetch"),
>       v.literal("extract"),
>       v.literal("analyze"),
>       v.literal("compile"),
>       v.literal("review")
>     ),
>     status: v.union(
>       v.literal("queued"),
>       v.literal("running"),
>       v.literal("completed"),
>       v.literal("failed")
>     ),
>     errorMessage: v.optional(v.string()),
>     retryCount: v.number(),
>   })
>     .index("by_userId", ["userId"])
>     .index("by_status", ["status"]),
> 
>   // Profile page analytics
>   profileViews: defineTable({
>     userId: v.id("users"),
>     viewedAt: v.number(),
>     referrer: v.optional(v.string()),
>     isAgentRead: v.boolean(),           // true if accessed via API/JSON, false if web page view
>   })
>     .index("by_userId", ["userId"])
>     .index("by_userId_date", ["userId", "viewedAt"]),
> });
> ```
> 
> **Why Convex over Postgres:**
> - Reactive queries mean the editor/dashboard gets real-time updates when pipeline jobs complete — no polling.
> - Scheduled functions replace BullMQ/Redis for job queue. One less infra dependency.
> - File storage is built in. No separate S3/R2 config.
> - TypeScript-native schema means type safety from DB to frontend with zero codegen.
> - Convex actions (for calling external APIs like Apify, OpenRouter) run in a serverless environment with automatic retries.
> 
> ### 4.4 Ingestion Pipeline (Detailed)
> 
> The ingestion pipeline is the core differentiator. It takes a URL, scrapes it, extracts structured data, generates analysis, and compiles the identity bundle.
>
