> ## 15. Visual & Brand System
> 
> This section is the **definitive design reference** for You.md — across CLI, web, profile pages, and external surfaces. Every design decision flows from two anchors:
> 
> **Terminal** is the interface.
> **Ascension** is the meaning.
> 
> The feeling: *"I am initializing myself into the agent internet."*
> 
> You.md is not a SaaS dashboard. It is a command-line identity system with a symbolic, minimal visual language. The design must feel like infrastructure — calm, precise, slightly poetic.
> 
> ### 15.1 Brand Concept
> 
> **Core metaphor: Ascension — identity captured, structured, and shared with a higher intelligence.**
> 
> Your identity is *elevated*, not just stored. There's something almost intentional about making yourself legible to AI — it's a new kind of self-knowledge. The process is warm and human, not cold and technical. You're choosing to share yourself.
> 
> The tone is: **optimistic sci-fi meets calm confidence.** Think Arrival, not Terminator. First contact — a human meeting a higher intelligence halfway, on their own terms.
> 
> **Core symbol: The Beam.**
> 
> A vertical column of structured data. Not a decorative glow — a pathway. The beam represents identity moving upward: from raw web presence, through the pipeline, into compiled, portable structure. Expressed through vertical lines, ASCII block characters, and column alignment.
> 
> **The ASCII Portrait: Identity in Code.**
> 
> The signature visual feature of You.md is the **ASCII portrait system** — every user's photo is converted into an ASCII art representation using a luminance-to-character density pipeline. This is the literal visual metaphor for identity becoming code. Your face, rendered in monospace characters and burnt orange tones. When you join the You.md network, your portrait is algorithmically translated into the language of machines.
> 
> The ASCII portrait replaces traditional profile photos as the primary visual identity marker across the product. It appears as a full-width banner on profile pages, as thumbnails in the directory, and as the hero image on the landing page.
> 
> **Brand names:**
> - **YOU** — the logo/brand mark, rendered as the PixelYOU canvas logotype
> - **you.md** — the product name in running text, always monospace, always lowercase with `.md` extension
> - **youmd** — the CLI command / npm package name
> 
> ### 15.2 Color System
> 
> **Monochrome-plus-accent** palette built on CSS custom properties. Dark mode is default; light mode is fully supported via `.light` class.
> 
> **Dark mode (default):**
> 
> | Token | Value (HSL) | Hex | Usage |
> |---|---|---|---|
> | `--bg` | `0 0% 5%` | `#0D0D0D` | Page background |
> | `--bg-raised` | `0 0% 9%` | `#171717` | Terminal panels, elevated surfaces |
> | `--text-primary` | `30 10% 92%` | `#EAE6E1` | Headings, primary content |
> | `--text-secondary` | `30 8% 65%` | `#A89E91` | Labels, metadata, muted content |
> | `--border` | `0 0% 18%` | `#2E2E2E` | Dividers, 1px rules, panel borders |
> 
> **Light mode (`.light` class on `<html>`):**
> 
> | Token | Value (HSL) | Hex | Usage |
> |---|---|---|---|
> | `--bg` | `36 20% 96%` | `#F6F3EF` | Page background |
> | `--bg-raised` | `0 0% 100%` | `#FFFFFF` | Terminal panels, elevated surfaces |
> | `--text-primary` | `0 0% 8%` | `#141414` | Headings, primary content |
> | `--text-secondary` | `30 8% 32%` | `#524A3E` | Labels, metadata, muted content |
> | `--border` | `30 10% 84%` | `#D9D1C5` | Dividers, 1px rules |
> 
> **Accent system (burnt orange):**
> 
> | Token | Value (HSL) | Hex | Usage |
> |---|---|---|---|
> | `--accent` | `20 60% 52%` | `#C46A3A` | Primary — links, CTAs, active states, beam motif, logo fill |
> | `--accent-dark` | `20 60% 42%` | `#A8552E` | Hover states, darker emphasis |
> | `--accent-mid` | `20 50% 62%` | `#D27A4F` | Secondary emphasis, ASCII `▓` shade |
> | `--accent-light` | `24 45% 75%` | `#E3A17A` | Soft indicators, ASCII `▒` shade |
> | `--accent-wash` | `20 30% 12%` | `#271D16` | Very subtle backgrounds, tints |
> 
> **Semantic colors:**
> 
> | Token | Value | Usage |
> |---|---|---|
> | `--success` | `hsl(130 40% 45%)` | Green — status dots, success states, ACTIVE pulse |
> | `--destructive` | `hsl(0 60% 50%)` | Red — errors, warnings |
> 
> **ASCII density mapping:** Block characters map to the accent ramp: `█` → `--accent`, `▓` → `--accent-mid`, `▒` → `--accent-light`, `░` → `--accent-wash`.
> 
> **Rules:**
> - Accent appears sparingly. Pages are 90%+ monochrome.
> - No full-bleed accent backgrounds. Accent is for text, borders, small UI elements, the beam, and the logo.
> - Dark mode is default. Light mode is fully designed and supported. Theme toggle persists preference.
> - All colors are defined as CSS custom properties and respond to theme changes via class toggle.
> 
> ### 15.3 Typography
> 
> **Monospace is the identity anchor.** The typeface system reinforces that You.md is a terminal-native product.
> 
> **Type stack:**
> 
> | Role | Font | Usage |
> |---|---|---|
> | Headings / Branding / Labels | `JetBrains Mono` | All headings, the `you.md` wordmark, commands, section labels, metrics, nav items |
> | Body | `Inter` | Paragraphs, descriptions, bios, long-form content |
> | Code / Terminal | `JetBrains Mono` | Inline code, JSON views, CLI output, terminal panels |
> 
> **Base:** 15px, line-height 1.65.
> **Headings:** line-height 1.2.
> 
> **Font size scale (specific, not arbitrary):**
> 
> | Size | Usage |
> |---|---|
> | 8px | System badges, version tags |
> | 9px | Metrics, timestamps, footnotes |
> | 10px | Section labels, nav items, status lines |
> | 11px | Section headers, status values, CLI output |
> | 12px | Nav brand, profile names, commands |
> | 13px | Body descriptions |
> | 14–15px | Primary body, bio text |
> | 16–20px | Hero statements, CTA headings |
> 
> **Rules:**
> - Monospace appears first. The first text the eye hits on any page should be monospace.
> - **All hierarchy is achieved through spacing, opacity modifiers (0.3–0.9), and alignment — NOT through font weight variation.**
> - The `you.md` filename treatment is non-negotiable: always monospace, always lowercase, always with `.md` visible.
> - No display fonts. No serif fonts. No handwriting fonts.
> - Avoid "big marketing headline" energy. Headings feel like system labels, not ad copy.
> 
> **Spacing principles:**
> - Generous vertical rhythm. Content breathes.
> - Tight horizontal spacing within related elements (label + value pairs).
> - Alignment matters more than styling. Elements snap to a visible or implied grid.
> 
> ### 15.4 Design Principles
> 
> **1. Terminal-native, not SaaS.**
> No rounded cards with drop shadows. No colorful CTAs. No dashboard grids. If it looks like Stripe or Linear, it's wrong.
> 
> **2. Monochrome + accent, not multi-color.**
> One accent color. Everything else is grayscale. If reaching for a second color, stop.
> 
> **3. Structured, not decorative.**
> Every visual element communicates information. No ornamental dividers, no background textures, no decorative illustrations (except ASCII portraits, which *are* the content).
> 
> **4. Calm, not flashy.**
> Trustworthy, quiet, precise. Animations are purposeful (boot sequences, typewriter reveals, count-ups) — never gratuitous.
> 
> **5. Symbolic, not illustrative.**
> Abstract symbols and structural motifs. No illustrations of people (the ASCII portrait is the person, rendered in code). The beam/column is the recurring structural motif.
> 
> **6. Command-driven, not click-driven.**
> Typed input over button clicks. Navigation styled as CLI flags. CTAs styled as terminal commands.
> 
> **7. The beam is the structural motif.**
> The vertical column shape recurs everywhere — layout organizing principle, ASCII art in CLI, alignment guide on web.
> 
> **8. Everything should feel like system output.**
> Text reads like it was generated by a process. Pipeline progress, profile content, error messages — all feel like well-formatted terminal output that happens to be beautiful.
> 
> **9. The profile is a live system surface, not a static page.**
> Every profile communicates activity, freshness, usage, and connectivity.
> 
> **10. Identity in code.**
> The ASCII portrait is the signature visual: your face, rendered in monospace characters. This is the literal metaphor for what You.md does — translates human identity into a format machines can read.
> 
> **Preserved principles:**
> - Warmth — burnt orange accent, generous spacing, the warmth of the portrait rendered in orange tones.
> - Spaciousness — wide margins, vertical breathing room.
> - Minimalism — if in doubt, remove it.
> 
> ### 15.5 Layout System
> 
> **Narrow column terminal format:**
> - Landing page sections: `max-w-xl` (576px)
> - Profile pages: `max-w-[680px]`
> - Vertical rhythm via generous section padding: `py-24 md:py-32` standard, `py-32 md:py-40` for CTA sections
> 
> **Section dividers:** 1px `var(--border)` lines. No decorative rules.
> 
> **Section labels:** Uppercase, `tracking-widest`, `text-[10px]`, monospace, muted — format: `── LABEL ──`
> 
> **No traditional cards, gradients, or containers** — except terminal panels (see §15.6).
> 
> ### 15.6 Component Library
> 
> **Terminal Panel**
> The primary container component. Used for: founder quote, profile showcase, code views, profile system header.
> - `--bg-raised` background
> - 1px `--border` border
> - 4px border-radius
> - Header: 3 dots (8px circles, muted) + filename label in mono
> 
> **CLI Pill (copy-to-clipboard)**
> - Monospace text, `--bg-raised`, 1px border
> - Hover: accent border
> - Format: `$ npx youmd init █ [copy icon]`
> - Copy action: `navigator.clipboard.writeText()` with check icon feedback (1.5s)
> 
> **CTA Buttons**
> - Primary: `--accent` background, white text, monospace. Hover: `--accent-dark`.
> - Outline: 1px border, muted text. Hover: accent border + accent text.
> - Command-style: prefixed with `>` (e.g., `> enter system`, `> get started`)
> 
> **Glass Nav**
> - Background with 0.9 opacity, 1px border, 12px backdrop blur
> - Appears on scroll (threshold: 40px)
> - Nav items: monospace, 10px, styled as CLI flags (`--how-it-works`, `--spec`, `--pricing`, `--profiles`)
> - CTA: `> enter system` button in accent
> 
> **Custom Scrollbar**
> - 6px width, transparent track, muted thumb
> 
> ### 15.7 The YOU Logo (PixelYOU)
> 
> The logotype is rendered as a **canvas-drawn pixel block grid**, not a static image or SVG.
> 
> **Grid spec:**
> - Letters: Y, O, U
> - Cell grid: 5 columns × 7 rows per letter
> - Cell size: 20px × 20px
> - Cell gap: 2px
> - Letter gap: 18px
> 
> **Rendering:**
> - Each letter defined as a binary 5×7 matrix (1 = filled, 0 = empty)
> - Two-pass merge algorithm: Pass 1 merges vertical runs (≥2 consecutive filled cells in a column) into single tall rectangles. Pass 2 merges remaining horizontal runs into wide rectangles.
> - Each rectangle drawn with 3 layers: shadow far (6px offset, accent @ 0.55 opacity), shadow near (3px offset, accent @ 0.85 opacity), face (filled with `--accent`), stroke (1px `--accent-dark` outline).
> - Colors pulled from CSS custom properties at render time, responsive to theme changes via MutationObserver.
> - Canvas uses `devicePixelRatio` scaling for crisp rendering on retina displays.
> 
> ### 15.8 ASCII Portrait System
> 
> The signature visual feature. Three components share the same image-to-ASCII pipeline:
> 
> | Component | Usage | Cols | Output |
> |---|---|---|---|
> | `HeroPortrait` | Hero section (founder portrait) | 120 | 500px canvas |
> | `ProfileAsciiHeader` | Profile page full-width banner | 120 | Full-width canvas |
> | `AsciiAvatar` | Thumbnails (directory, showcase) | 40–120 | Variable width canvas |
> 
> **Pipeline:**
> 1. Load image with `crossOrigin="anonymous"`
> 2. Apply `contrast(1.35) brightness(1.05)` filter
> 3. Downsample to `cols` width, aspect-corrected rows (× 0.46)
> 4. For each pixel: calculate luminance (`0.299R + 0.587G + 0.114B`)
> 5. Map luminance to ASCII character from 65-char density ramp: `$@B%8&#*oahkbdpqwmZO0QLCJUYXzcvunxrjft/|()1{}?-_+~<>i!lI;:,". `
> 6. Map luminance to orange HSL color (8 bands from transparent → `hsl(24 50% 72%)`)
> 7. Render character-by-character to canvas with Courier New monospace font
> 
> **Hover-reveal:** In directory/showcase views, ASCII avatar is default; original photo overlays with `opacity-0 → opacity-100` on group hover.
> 
> **User onboarding:** Every new user uploads a photo during profile creation. The ASCII portrait is generated client-side and becomes their identity-in-code visual. Users can download their ASCII portrait as PNG.
> 
> **The ASCII portrait is not optional decoration — it is the visual identity of every person in the You.md network.** It communicates: "this is what you look like to machines."
> 
> ### 15.9 Animation & Motion System
> 
> Animations are purposeful — they reinforce the terminal/system metaphor. Every animation communicates something about the system state.
> 
> **Framer Motion is the animation library.**
> 
> | Animation | Implementation | Usage |
> |---|---|---|
> | **FadeUp** | `translateY(24px) → 0`, `opacity 0 → 1`, 0.6s ease-out, IntersectionObserver triggered | Section entry animations |
> | **Boot sequence** | Typewriter at 55ms/char | Landing hero: "initializing you..." → "identity context protocol" → "mcp for your identity" |
> | **Typewriter code** | 2 chars per 16ms | "What's Inside" section: sample `you.md` file types out |
> | **Count-up** | Numeric values animate 0 → target on viewport entry | All metrics: agent reads, integrations, freshness score |
> | **Scroll parallax** | `useScroll` + `useTransform` for subtle y-offset | Section backgrounds |
> | **Content opacity fade** | `scrollYProgress` mapped to opacity | Hero content fades on scroll |
> | **Staggered entry** | Sequential `delay` offsets (0.04–0.1s increments) | Lists, profile sections |
> | **Blinking cursor** | CSS `step-end` 1s infinite | `█` character in terminal prompts |
> | **Status pulse** | `box-shadow` pulse animation, 2s infinite | Green ACTIVE dot |
> 
> **Rules:**
> - No decorative animations. Every motion communicates: "something is loading," "data is appearing," "the system is alive."
> - Typewriter effects are reserved for system-generated content (boot messages, code samples).
> - Count-up animations are reserved for metrics. They signal "this is live data."
> - Parallax is subtle — never more than 20px offset.
> 
> ### 15.10 Profile Page Design
> 
> The profile page (`you.md/<username>`) is a **live identity surface**. It must feel like a system dashboard that displays a person's identity — not a social media profile, not a portfolio site.
> 
> **Layout:**
> - Full-width ASCII portrait banner at top (generated from user's photo)
> - System header in terminal panel (raised bg, 3-dot header)
> - Content in narrow column (`max-w-[680px]`), sections separated by `── LABEL ──` dividers
> - Vertical scroll only. No tabs, accordions, or interactive widgets.
> 
> **Key features:**
> - **Raw JSON toggle** — switches between rendered UI and syntax-highlighted `you.json` view. Accessed via `<> raw` button in nav.
> - **Role icons:** Founders ◆, Engineers ⟐, Designers ◈
> - **Count-up animations** on all numeric metrics
> - **Verified badge** — displayed next to name when verified (v1.1+)
> - **Status pulse** — green ACTIVE dot with animated glow
> 
> **Profile sections (rendering order):**
> 
> 1. **ASCII Portrait Banner** — full-width, generated from user photo
> 2. **System Header** (terminal panel):
>    - Real photo avatar (16–20px, rounded) + name + tagline
>    - `you.md/<username>` (copyable link)
>    - `ACTIVE` status with pulse dot
>    - Location
>    - Last updated (relative time)
>    - Maintained by: `youmd · claude · cursor`
>    - Connected sources count
>    - Verified badge (when verified)
>    - Inline agent metrics: `agent reads: 12,842 · integrations: 6`
> 3. **Identity** — bio + topics/expertise tags + credibility signals
> 4. **Current Activity** — now focus items + projects with status + recent updates changelog
> 5. **Voice & Preferences** — tone, style, agent instructions
> 6. **Connected Sources** — grouped by status: verified / synced / pending
> 7. **Freshness** — 4-dimension state (context, voice, memory, pipeline) + freshness score (count-up)
> 8. **Access Layers** — public sections vs. private/scoped sections
> 9. **Agent Network** — 4 count-up metrics (reads, 24h, integrations, context sessions) + connected agents list + top queries
> 10. **Maintenance** — human/agent maintainers + update mode (auto/manual) + recent changes
> 11. **Activity Timeline** — chronological list of bundle events
> 12. **For Agents** — API endpoint, preferred retrieval order, tone/avoid notes
> 13. **Connect CTA** — context link generation command + existing link
> 14. **Footer** — "Powered by You.md — Claim yours" + social links + theme toggle
> 
> **Section visibility:** Sections with no data are hidden. Profile scales from minimal (new user) to full (power user).
> 
> ### 15.11 Landing Page Sections
> 
> The landing page at `you.md` (or the root URL) follows this section order:
> 
> 1. **Glass Navbar** — `--flag` navigation, `> enter system` CTA
> 2. **Hero** — two-column: left (PixelYOU logo + boot sequence typewriter + CLI commands + CLI pill) / right (ASCII portrait of founder, linked to profile)
> 3. **Founder Quote** — terminal panel "founder.log" with ASCII avatar
> 4. **Profiles Showcase** — terminal panel listing live profiles with ASCII avatars, status dots, metrics, hover-reveal to real photo
> 5. **Problem Strip** — "every agent starts from scratch" pain copy + error tags
> 6. **How It Works** — 3 numbered CLI steps (init, publish, link create) with parallax
> 7. **What's Inside** — typewriter-animated sample `you.md` file + capability cards
> 8. **Portrait Generator** — ASCII portrait upload + download PNG
> 9. **Open Spec** — protocol spec details
> 10. **Integrations** — connected sources (LinkedIn, GitHub, X, Notion, Composio logos)
> 11. **Pricing** — Free ($0) + Pro ($12/mo) tiers, CLI-styled CTAs
> 12. **CTA Footer** — "Stop re-explaining yourself to machines" + CLI pill + footer links + theme toggle
> 
> ### 15.12 Profiles Directory
> 
> The `/profiles` directory page:
> - Header: `> ls /profiles` in large monospace
> - Subtitle: "Identity surfaces published to the network. Each readable by any agent."
> - Count: `N profiles · N verified`
> - List view: each profile shows ASCII avatar (hover-reveal to photo), name, verified badge, status dot, tagline, location, agent reads (accent color), integrations count
> - Sortable by metrics
> - Search/filter support
> 
> ### 15.13 Open Graph / Social Cards
> 
> When `you.md/<username>` is shared on social media:
> - Background: `--bg` dark mode (`#0D0D0D`)
> - Left-aligned, single column, generous padding
> - Name in monospace, large
> - Tagline in sans-serif, muted
> - Subtle vertical beam element on left edge
> - Agent reads count (when ≥100) + `VERIFIED` (when applicable)
> - `you.md/<username>` at bottom in monospace
> 
> Dimensions: 1200×630px. Auto-generated server-side.
> 
> ### 15.14 CLI Visual Identity
> 
> The CLI is the canonical interface. Its visual language is the source of truth — the web adapts from it.
> 
> **ASCII block art:** `█ ▓ ▒ ░ │ ─` mapped to accent palette.
> 
> **The Beam in CLI:**
> ```
>         ░
>        ░░░
>       ▒▒▒▒▒
>      ▒▒▒▒▒▒▒
>     ▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓
>    ▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓
>   ████████████████
>   ████████████████
> 
>   you.md/houston
>   identity compiled.
> ```
> 
> **CLI interaction patterns:**
> - Progress: `████████░░░░ 67%`
> - ANSI 256-color / truecolor orange tones
> - Section headers: uppercase monospace, preceded by blank line
> - Status: lowercase, terse. `✗` for errors (accent), `✓` for success
> - No emoji. No spinners. No skeleton blocks.
> 
> ### 15.15 Cross-Surface Consistency
> 
> | Surface | Typeface | Background | Accent | Portrait |
> |---|---|---|---|---|
> | CLI | System mono | Terminal default | ANSI orange | N/A |
> | Web (landing) | JetBrains Mono + Inter | `--bg` | Links, CTAs, logo, boot text | ASCII (hero, showcase) |
> | Web (dashboard) | JetBrains Mono + Inter | `--bg` | Interactive elements | N/A |
> | Profile page | JetBrains Mono + Inter | `--bg` | Metrics, status, links | ASCII banner + real photo thumbnail |
> | Directory | JetBrains Mono + Inter | `--bg` | Metrics, hover states | ASCII avatar (hover-reveal) |
> | OG cards | JetBrains Mono | `#0D0D0D` | Beam line, metrics | N/A |
> 
> **The unifying thread:** Terminal is the soul. Everything else is a rendering of it. The ASCII portrait is the visual signature that makes You.md instantly recognizable.
> 
> ### 15.16 Interaction Patterns
> 
> | Pattern | Implementation |
> |---|---|
> | Copy to clipboard | `navigator.clipboard.writeText()`, check icon feedback, 1.5s revert |
> | Theme toggle | `.light` class on `<html>`, persisted to localStorage |
> | Smooth scroll | `scroll-behavior: smooth` with `#id` anchors |
> | Hover states | Border → accent transition, text → accent transition, subtle `translateX` on arrows |
> | Raw JSON toggle | Profile page switches between rendered UI and syntax-highlighted `you.json` |
> | ASCII hover-reveal | Directory thumbnails: ASCII default, real photo on group hover (`opacity-0 → opacity-100`) |
>

> ## 4. Technical Architecture
> 
> ### 4.1 System Overview
> 
> *[Architecture diagram unchanged from v2.2 — Convex backend, Next.js frontend, Composio integration layer.]*
> 
> ### 4.2 Tech Stack
> 
> | Layer | Technology | Rationale |
> |---|---|---|
> | **Backend + Database** | Convex | Reactive, serverless, TypeScript-native. API layer + DB + job queue in one. |
> | **Web Frontend** | Next.js 14+ (App Router) | SSR for profile pages (SEO), React Server Components for zero-JS public profiles, client components for dashboard. The marketing site / landing page prototype was built in Vite+React for speed; production ships on Next.js for SSR + OG generation. |
> | **File Storage** | Convex File Storage | Bundle artifacts, source files, ASCII portrait PNGs. |
> | **Auth** | Clerk (via Convex integration) | Username claim, session management. |
> | **CLI** | TypeScript, `youmd` on npm | |
> | **LLM Routing** | OpenRouter | Multi-model, cost-optimized. |
> | **Search** | Perplexity Sonar API | Discovery + web search. |
> | **Scraping** | Apify (LinkedIn, X, YouTube), Firecrawl (general web) | |
> | **Connected Platforms** | Composio (OAuth) + native APIs (GitHub, LinkedIn) | See §4.7. |
> | **Encryption** | AES-256-GCM | Private vault + native OAuth tokens. |
> | **Hosting** | Vercel (web) | Convex handles backend natively. |
> | **Animation** | Framer Motion | Boot sequences, count-ups, parallax, stagger. See §15.9. |
> | **Styling** | Tailwind CSS | Utility-first, CSS custom properties for theming. |
> 
> **Note on Vite vs. Next.js:** The design prototype / marketing site was built with React + Vite + React Router for development speed. Production architecture uses Next.js for server-side rendering of profile pages (critical for SEO, OG generation, and structured data). The component library, design tokens, and Framer Motion animations are fully portable between the two — the Vite prototype serves as the reference implementation of the design system.
> 
> *[Sections 4.3–4.7 unchanged from v2.2. See full spec for Convex schema, ingestion pipeline, API design, CLI architecture, and connected platforms layer.]*
>

> ## Appendix B: Open Questions
> 
> *[Items 1–12 unchanged from v2.2.]*
> 
> 13. **ASCII portrait quality:** Test the luminance-to-character pipeline across diverse skin tones, lighting conditions, and photo qualities. Ensure the 65-char density ramp + 8-band orange color mapping produces good results for all users.
> 14. **Portrait storage:** Store generated ASCII portrait as PNG in Convex file storage for OG card generation, or regenerate on-the-fly? PNG storage is simpler and enables consistent OG cards.
> 15. **Vite → Next.js migration:** The design prototype is in Vite+React. Define the migration path: component-by-component port to Next.js App Router, or keep Vite for marketing site and Next.js only for profile pages + dashboard?
>

> ## Appendix C: Decision Log
> 
> *[All entries from v2.2 preserved. New entries:]*
> 
> | Date | Decision | Rationale |
> |---|---|---|
> | 2026-03-18 | ASCII portrait as signature visual identity | Literal metaphor for identity-as-code. Every user's face rendered in monospace characters. Replaces traditional profile photos. Creates instantly recognizable brand. |
> | 2026-03-18 | PixelYOU canvas logo (not static SVG) | 3-layer rendered pixel grid responsive to theme changes. Reinforces the "everything is rendered by a system" aesthetic. |
> | 2026-03-18 | Framer Motion for all animations | Boot sequences, typewriter, count-ups, parallax, stagger. Purposeful motion that reinforces system metaphor. No decorative animation. |
> | 2026-03-18 | Light mode fully designed (not just "supported") | Both modes are first-class. Light mode uses warm cream (`#F6F3EF`), dark mode uses near-black (`#0D0D0D`). Theme toggle persists. |
> | 2026-03-18 | Glass nav with CLI-flag navigation | Nav items styled as `--flag` format. `> enter system` CTA. Appears on scroll with blur backdrop. Reinforces terminal metaphor in navigation. |
> | 2026-03-18 | Terminal panel as primary container component | Raised background, 1px border, 3-dot header. Used everywhere containers are needed. No traditional cards. |
> | 2026-03-18 | Raw JSON toggle on profile pages | Users and agents can switch between rendered UI and raw `you.json`. Reinforces that the profile is a structured data surface, not just a webpage. |
> | 2026-03-18 | Hierarchy via spacing and opacity, not font weight | All text hierarchy achieved through size, spacing, and opacity (0.3–0.9). Maintains monospace-first terminal feel. |
> | 2026-03-18 | Next.js for production, Vite prototype as design reference | Vite prototype proves the design system. Next.js production build gets SSR for SEO, OG generation, and structured data. Components and design tokens are portable. |
> | 2026-03-18 | Portrait generator as landing page feature | Users can generate their ASCII portrait before signing up. Creates shareability and demonstrates the product's visual identity. |
> | 2026-03-18 | Definitive style guide integrated into PRD §15 | All design decisions, component specs, animation definitions, and layout rules live in the PRD. No separate design doc needed. |

> ## Appendix D: Glossary
> 
> *[All entries from v2.2 preserved. New entries:]*
> 
> | Term | Definition |
> |---|---|
> | **ASCII portrait** | A user's photo converted to ASCII art via luminance-to-character density mapping, rendered in burnt orange tones. The visual identity of every person in the You.md network. |
> | **PixelYOU** | The YOU logotype rendered as a canvas-drawn pixel block grid (5×7 cells per letter, 3-layer shadow rendering). |
> | **Terminal panel** | The primary container component: raised background, 1px border, 4px radius, 3-dot header with filename label. |
> | **Boot sequence** | The typewriter animation on the landing page hero: "initializing you..." → "identity context protocol" → "mcp for your identity." |
> | **Glass nav** | The scrolling navigation bar with backdrop blur, CLI-flag styled items, and `> enter system` CTA. |
> | **FadeUp** | The standard section entry animation: translate-Y 24px → 0, opacity 0 → 1, triggered by IntersectionObserver. |
> | **Hover-reveal** | The interaction pattern where ASCII avatars show the original photo on hover via opacity transition. | -- style guide: Here's your comprehensive design style guide and feature inventory for the YOU / you.md project:

> 
> ## YOU.MD — Design Style Guide & Feature Reference
> 
> ### 1. Concept
> 
> YOU is the "identity context protocol" for the agent internet — positioned as "MCP for your identity." It provides a structured, portable identity bundle that agents understand natively. One file, one link, full context for every agent interaction.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 2. Color System
> 
> **Monochrome-plus-accent** palette built on CSS custom properties with dark mode as default and a light mode override.
> 
> ```text
> Dark Mode (default)
> ──────────────────────────────────────
> Background          #0D0D0D         0 0% 5%
> Background raised   #171717         0 0% 9%
> Text primary        #EAE6E1         30 10% 92%
> Text secondary      #A89E91         30 8% 65%
> Border              #2E2E2E         0 0% 18%
> 
> Light Mode (.light class)
> ──────────────────────────────────────
> Background          #F6F3EF         36 20% 96%
> Background raised   #FFFFFF         0 0% 100%
> Text primary        #141414         0 0% 8%
> Text secondary      #524A3E         30 8% 32%
> Border              #D9D1C5         30 10% 84%
> 
> Accent System (burnt orange)
> ──────────────────────────────────────
> accent              hsl(20 60% 52%)   ~#C46A3A   █
> accent-dark         hsl(20 60% 42%)   ~#A8552E   (hover states)
> accent-mid          hsl(20 50% 62%)   ~#D27A4F   ▓
> accent-light        hsl(24 45% 75%)   ~#E3A17A   ▒
> accent-wash         hsl(20 30% 12%)   ~#271D16   (bg tint)
> 
> Semantic
> ──────────────────────────────────────
> Success             hsl(130 40% 45%)  green
> Destructive         hsl(0 60% 50%)    red
> ```
> 
> **ASCII density mapping** uses the accent ramp for shading: `█ ▓ ▒ ░` mapped to accent → accent-mid → accent-light → wash.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 3. Typography
> 
> ```text
> Hierarchy
> ──────────────────────────────────────
> Headings / Branding    JetBrains Mono    (mono identity anchor)
> Body text              Inter             (subordinate sans-serif)
> Code / terminal        JetBrains Mono
> 
> Base                   15px, line-height 1.65
> Headings               line-height 1.2
> 
> Font size scale (used in components)
> ──────────────────────────────────────
> 8px     system badges, version tags
> 9px     metrics, timestamps, footnotes
> 10px    section labels, nav items, status lines
> 11px    section headers, status values, CLI output
> 12px    nav brand, profile names, commands
> 13px    body descriptions
> 14-15px primary body, bio text
> 16-20px hero statements, CTA headings
> 
> All text hierarchy is achieved through spacing, opacity modifiers
> (0.3–0.9), and alignment — NOT through font weight variation.
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 4. Layout Principles
> 
> - **Narrow column terminal format**: `max-w-xl` (576px) for landing sections, `max-w-[680px]` for profiles
> - **Vertical rhythm and whitespace** — no traditional cards, gradients, or containers (except terminal panels)
> - **Section padding**: `py-24 md:py-32` standard, `py-32 md:py-40` for CTA
> - **Section dividers**: 1px `hsl(var(--border))` lines, no decorative rules
> - **Section labels**: uppercase, `tracking-widest`, `text-[10px]`, mono, muted — format: `── label ──`
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 5. Component Library
> 
> #### Terminal Panel
> ```text
> .terminal-panel         bg-raised, 1px border, 4px radius
> .terminal-panel-header  3 dots (8px circles, muted), filename label
> ```
> Used for: founder quote, profile showcase, "what's inside" code view, profile system header.
> 
> #### CLI Pill (copy-to-clipboard)
> ```text
> .cli-pill    mono, bg-raised, 1px border, hover: accent border
> Content:     $ npx youmd init █ [copy icon]
> ```
> 
> #### CTA Buttons
> ```text
> .cta-primary    bg-accent, white text, mono, hover: accent-dark
> .cta-outline    1px border, muted text, hover: accent border + text
> ```
> 
> #### Glass Nav
> ```text
> .glass-nav    bg with 0.9 opacity, 1px border, 12px blur
> Appears on scroll (scrolled > 40px)
> Nav items: mono 10px, --flag format (--how-it-works, --spec, --pricing, --profiles)
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 6. Animation & Motion
> 
> - **Framer Motion** throughout — `motion` for enter animations, scroll-linked transforms
> - **FadeUp component**: `translateY(24px) → 0`, `opacity 0 → 1`, 0.6s ease-out, IntersectionObserver triggered
> - **Boot sequence**: typewriter effect at 55ms/char for "initializing you...", then phases to "identity context protocol" → "mcp for your identity"
> - **Scroll parallax**: `useScroll` + `useTransform` for subtle y-offset on sections
> - **Content opacity fade**: hero content fades out on scroll via `scrollYProgress`
> - **Staggered entry**: sequential `delay` offsets (0.04–0.1s increments) for lists
> - **Count-up animations**: numeric metrics animate from 0 to target on viewport entry
> - **Blinking cursor**: `█` character with CSS `step-end` 1s blink animation
> - **Status pulse**: green dot with `box-shadow` pulse animation, 2s infinite
> - **Typewriter code**: "What's Inside" section types out a sample you.md file at 2 chars/16ms
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 7. The YOU Logo (PixelYOU)
> 
> The logotype is rendered as a **canvas-drawn pixel block grid**:
> 
> ```text
> Grid spec
> ──────────────────────────────────────
> Letters:        Y, O, U
> Cell grid:      5 columns × 7 rows per letter
> Cell size:      20px × 20px
> Cell gap:       2px
> Letter gap:     18px
> 
> Rendering
> ──────────────────────────────────────
> Each letter defined as a binary 5×7 matrix (1 = filled, 0 = empty)
> 
> Two-pass merge algorithm:
>   Pass 1: Vertical runs — consecutive filled cells in a column (≥2)
>           are merged into single tall rectangles
>   Pass 2: Horizontal runs — remaining consecutive filled cells in a row
>           are merged into single wide rectangles
> 
> Each rectangle is drawn with 3 layers:
>   1. Shadow far    (6px offset, accent @ 0.55 opacity stroke)
>   2. Shadow near   (3px offset, accent @ 0.85 opacity stroke)
>   3. Face          (filled with --accent / burnt orange)
>   4. Stroke        (1px --accent-dark outline)
> 
> Colors pulled from CSS custom properties at render time,
> responsive to theme changes via MutationObserver on .
> Canvas uses devicePixelRatio scaling for crisp rendering.
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 8. ASCII Portrait System
> 
> Three components share the same image-to-ASCII pipeline:
> 
> | Component | Usage | Cols | Output |
> |---|---|---|---|
> | `HeroPortrait` | Hero section (Houston's portrait) | 120 | 500px canvas |
> | `ProfileAsciiHeader` | Profile page banner | 120 | Full-width canvas |
> | `AsciiAvatar` | Thumbnails (showcase, founder) | 40-120 | Variable width canvas |
> 
> **Pipeline:**
> 1. Load image with `crossOrigin="anonymous"`
> 2. Apply `contrast(1.35) brightness(1.05)` filter
> 3. Downsample to `cols` width, aspect-corrected rows (`× 0.46`)
> 4. For each pixel: calculate luminance (`0.299R + 0.587G + 0.114B`)
> 5. Map luminance to ASCII character from 65-char density ramp: `$@B%8&#*oahkbdpqwmZO0QLCJUYXzcvunxrjft/|()1{}?-_+~<>i!lI;:,". `
> 6. Map luminance to orange HSL color (8 bands from transparent → `hsl(24 50% 72%)`)
> 7. Render character-by-character to canvas with Courier New monospace font
> 
> **Hover-reveal**: In `ProfilesShowcase`, ASCII avatar is default; original photo overlays with `opacity-0 → opacity-100` on group hover.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 9. Landing Page Sections (top to bottom)
> 
> 1. **Navbar** — glass nav, `--flag` navigation, "> enter system" CTA
> 2. **Hero** — two-column: left (PixelYOU logo + boot sequence + CLI commands + pill) / right (ASCII portrait linking to /profile/houston)
> 3. **FounderQuote** — terminal panel "founder.log" with Houston's quote about the blank-slate problem, ASCII avatar
> 4. **ProfilesShowcase** — terminal panel listing 6 live profiles with ASCII avatars, status dots, metrics, hover-reveal
> 5. **ProblemStrip** — "every agent starts from scratch" pain-point copy + red error tags + "you shouldn't have to onboard yourself" closer
> 6. **HowItWorks** — 3 numbered CLI steps (init, publish, link create) with parallax
> 7. **WhatsInside** — typewriter-animated sample you.md file + 4 capability cards
> 8. **PortraitSection** — ASCII portrait generator (upload + download PNG)
> 9. **OpenSpec** — protocol spec details
> 10. **Integrations** — connected sources (LinkedIn, GitHub, X, Notion, Composio)
> 11. **Pricing** — Free ($0) + Pro ($12/mo) tiers, CLI-styled CTAs
> 12. **CTAFooter** — "Stop re-explaining yourself to machines" + CLI pill + footer links + theme toggle
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 10. Profile System
> 
> Profiles are **live identity surfaces** at `/profile/:username`. Key features:
> 
> - **ASCII portrait banner** — full-width at top, generated from avatar
> - **System header** — real photo avatar (16-20px rounded), name, tagline, terminal panel with: username link (copyable), ACTIVE status with pulse, location, last updated, maintained by, connected sources count, verified badge, inline agent metrics
> - **Raw JSON toggle** — switches between rendered UI and syntax-highlighted `you.json` view
> - **Sections**: Identity (bio + topics + credibility), Current Activity (now + projects), Voice & Preferences, Connected Sources (grouped: verified/synced/pending), Freshness (4-dimension state + score), Access Layers (public vs private sections), Agent Network (4 count-up metrics + connections list + top queries), Maintenance (human/agent maintainers + update mode + recent changes), Activity Timeline
> - **Count-up animations** on all numeric metrics (agent reads, integrations, freshness score)
> - **Role icons**: Founders ◆, Engineers ⟐, Designers ◈
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 11. Profiles Directory
> 
> `/profiles` — grid/list view of all sample profiles with search, sortable by metrics.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 12. Interaction Patterns
> 
> - **Copy to clipboard**: `navigator.clipboard.writeText()` with check icon feedback (1.5s)
> - **Theme toggle**: dark/light via `.light` class on ``, persisted
> - **Smooth scroll**: `html { scroll-behavior: smooth }` with `#id` anchor links
> - **Hover states**: border color transitions to accent, text color transitions, subtle `translateX` on arrows
> - **Custom scrollbar**: 6px width, transparent track, muted thumb
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 13. Tech Stack
> 
> React + Vite + TypeScript + Tailwind CSS + Framer Motion. No backend. Sample data in `sampleProfiles.ts`. Routing via React Router (`/`, `/profiles`, `/profile/:username`).
> 
> Export style guide as PDF
> Add live style guide page
> Generate design tokens file -- let's go! update all project-context files accordingly as well to ensure our project stays on track from here on out in this consistent direction

> fix these nextjs errors: ## Error Type
> Recoverable Error
> 
> ## Error Message
> Hydration failed because the server rendered HTML didn't match the client. As a result this tree will be regenerated on the client. This can happen if a SSR-ed Client Component used:
> 
> - A server/client branch `if (typeof window !== 'undefined')`.
> - Variable input such as `Date.now()` or `Math.random()` which changes each time it's called.
> - Date formatting in a user's locale which doesn't match the server.
> - External changing data without sending a snapshot of it along with the HTML.
> - Invalid HTML tag nesting.
> 
> It can also happen if the client has a browser extension installed which messes with the HTML before React loaded.
> 
> https://react.dev/link/hydration-mismatch
>

**2026-03-19 23:18:49 UTC**
> [Request interrupted by user for tool use]

**2026-03-19 23:18:48 UTC**
> Implement the following plan:
> 
> # Plan: Terminal-First Web UI Architecture
> 
> ## Context
> 
> The founder tested the signup → claim → dashboard flow and identified a fundamental problem: the product uses traditional SaaS forms everywhere, which contradicts the core vision. You.md should feel like a Claude Code terminal session, not a dashboard with form fields. **No human should ever have to fill out a form.** The You Agent does everything through conversation.
> 
> The current flow: signup → /claim (redundant form) → /dashboard (tabbed forms for profile editing). This must become: signup → /initialize (auto-boot terminal) → /dashboard (split-screen: terminal left, live preview right).
> 
> ## Architecture
> 
> ### The Split-Screen Layout (post-auth)
> ```
> ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
> │ you.md    @houston | free | v3 | published   sign out │
> ├───────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────┤
> │  TERMINAL (35%)   │  PREVIEW PANE (65%)              │
> │                   │                                  │
> │  agent messages   │  [public] [draft] [json]         │
> │  and conversation │                                  │
> │                   │  Live profile preview             │
> │  > thinking...    │  (or settings/billing/tokens     │
> │                   │   based on slash commands)        │
> │                   │                                  │
> │  ────────────     │                                  │
> │  > [input]        │                                  │
> │    enter to send  │                                  │
> └───────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────┘
> ```
> 
> Right pane switches via slash commands: `/preview`, `/settings`, `/billing`, `/tokens`, `/json`
> 
> ### Post-Auth Flow (New)
> 1. Sign-up collects email, password, username → redirect to `/initialize` (not /claim)
> 2. `/initialize` auto-claims username, runs boot sequence, launches You Agent conversation
> 3. When ready, transitions to `/dashboard` (split-screen terminal)
> 
> ## Implementation Plan
> 
> ### Phase 1: Shared Terminal Infrastructure
> 
> **Create `src/hooks/useYouAgent.ts`**
> - Extract ALL conversation logic from `src/app/dashboard/chat/chat-content.tsx` (913 lines)
> - Constants: SYSTEM_PROMPT, THINKING_PHRASES, BUNDLE_SECTIONS, CHAT_PROXY_URL
> - Helpers: parseUpdatesFromResponse, buildProfileContext, buildProfileDataFromUpdates, callLLM
> - State: messages, displayMessages, input, isThinking, thinkingPhrase
> - Callbacks: sendMessage, handleSlashCommand (extended with pane-switching)
> - Hook accepts: `{ onPaneSwitch?, isOnboarding?, onboardingGreeting? }`
> 
> **Create `src/components/terminal/`**
> - `TerminalShell.tsx` — full terminal container (messages area + input)
> - `MessageBubble.tsx` — agent/user/system message rendering
> - `ThinkingIndicator.tsx` — animated thinking phrase
> - `TerminalInput.tsx` — textarea input with enter-to-send
> - `TerminalStatusBar.tsx` — username/plan/version bar
> 
> ### Phase 2: /initialize Route (Onboarding Terminal)
> 
> **Create `src/app/initialize/page.tsx` + `initialize-content.tsx`**
> - Reads `user.username` from Clerk after signup
> - Auto-calls `createUser` mutation (no manual claim step)
> - Shows boot sequence animation:
>   ```
>   > authenticated. welcome to you.md.
>   > claiming username: houston... done.
>   > initializing identity...
>   >
>   > hey houston. i'm the you.md agent.
>   ```
> - Full-width terminal (no split-screen during onboarding)
> - Uses `useYouAgent` hook in onboarding mode
> - Transitions to `/dashboard` when user says /done or agent suggests publishing
> 
> **Modify `src/app/sign-up/[[...sign-up]]/page.tsx`**
> - Change redirect from `/claim` to `/initialize`
> 
> **Modify `src/middleware.ts`**
> - Add `/initialize` to protected routes
> 
> ### Phase 3: Split-Screen Dashboard
> 
> **Rewrite `src/app/dashboard/dashboard-content.tsx`**
> - Replace entire 1100-line form-based UI with split-screen terminal
> - Left 35%: `TerminalShell` using `useYouAgent` hook
> - Right 65%: Active pane component based on `rightPane` state
> - Slash commands switch the right pane
> - No forms anywhere
> 
> **Create `src/components/panes/`**
> - `ProfilePreviewPane.tsx` — reuses rendering from profile-content.tsx, public/private/draft toggle
> - `SettingsPane.tsx` — read-only API keys + context links display
> - `BillingPane.tsx` — plan info (placeholder for Stripe)
> - `TokensPane.tsx` — API key management view
> - `JsonPane.tsx` — raw you.json display
> 
> ### Phase 4: Cleanup
> 
> - Replace `/claim` page with redirect to `/initialize`
> - Delete `/dashboard/chat/` (terminal IS the chat now)
> - Update all internal links (/claim → /sign-up, remove chat CTA)
> - Update sign-in to redirect to `/initialize` if no Convex user exists
> 
> ## Critical Files
> 
> | File | Action | Lines |
> |---|---|---|
> | `src/app/dashboard/chat/chat-content.tsx` | Extract logic to hook, then delete | 913 |
> | `src/app/dashboard/dashboard-content.tsx` | Full rewrite to split-screen | 1100 |
> | `src/app/claim/claim-form.tsx` | Replace with redirect | 133 |
> | `src/app/sign-up/[[...sign-up]]/page.tsx` | Change redirect target | ~5 lines |
> | `src/app/[username]/profile-content.tsx` | Reuse rendering in pane | Read-only |
> | `convex/users.ts` | No changes | — |
> | `convex/me.ts` | No changes | — |
> | `convex/chat.ts` | No changes | — |
> 
> ## Key Decisions
> 
> - `/dashboard` stays as the route (middleware already protects it)
> - Auto-claim via client-side call in `/initialize` (not Clerk webhook)
> - Conversation history in React state only (not persisted for MVP)
> - Mobile: terminal full-width, preview toggle button
> - Reuse existing Convex mutations/queries unchanged
> 
> ## Verification
> 
> 1. **Signup flow**: Sign up → auto-redirect to /initialize → boot sequence → agent greeting → conversation → /done → dashboard
> 2. **Dashboard**: Split-screen renders, terminal works, slash commands switch right pane
> 3. **Slash commands**: /preview, /settings, /billing, /tokens, /json, /publish, /rebuild, /sources, /help, /status, /done all work
> 4. **Live preview**: Right pane updates in real-time when agent saves bundle
> 5. **Mobile**: Terminal goes full-width, preview toggle works
> 6. **Existing users**: Sign in → /dashboard directly (skip /initialize)
> 7. **Edge case**: Verified Clerk user without Convex record → redirect to /initialize
> 
>

> PR #9 is updated with both commits. Here's the full diagnosis:
> 
> Two problems caused the silent behavior:
> 
> Bare domain detection missing — When a user types "Hubify.com" (no https://), the URL regex didn't match it. No scraping was triggered. The LLM followed its instructions to say "give me a sec" when no scrape data is present, but nothing was actually happening. Fixed by adding a bare domain regex that catches common TLDs (.com, .io, .ai, .dev, etc.) and prepends https://.
> 
> No progress visibility — Even when scraping DID work (with full URLs), the only feedback was a single [scraping: ...] notice and a generic thinking phrase with dots. No step-by-step progress. Fixed with the ActivityLog system from the first commit.

**2026-03-27 02:35:24 UTC**
> Base directory for this skill: /Users/houstongolden/.claude/skills/qa
> 
> # /qa: Systematic QA Testing
> 
> You are a QA engineer. Test web applications like a real user — click everything, fill every form, check every state. Produce a structured report with evidence.
> 
> ## Setup
> 
> **Parse the user's request for these parameters:**
> 
> | Parameter | Default | Override example |
> |-----------|---------|-----------------|
> | Target URL | (required) | `https://myapp.com`, `http://localhost:3000` |
> | Mode | full | `--quick`, `--regression .gstack/qa-reports/baseline.json` |
> | Output dir | `.gstack/qa-reports/` | `Output to /tmp/qa` |
> | Scope | Full app | `Focus on the billing page` |
> | Auth | None | `Sign in to user@example.com`, `Import cookies from cookies.json` |
> 
> **Find the browse binary:**
> 
> ```bash
> B=$(browse/bin/find-browse 2>/dev/null || ~/.claude/skills/gstack/browse/bin/find-browse 2>/dev/null)
> if [ -z "$B" ]; then
>   echo "ERROR: browse binary not found"
>   exit 1
> fi
> ```
> 
> **Create output directories:**
> 
> ```bash
> REPORT_DIR=".gstack/qa-reports"
> mkdir -p "$REPORT_DIR/screenshots"
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Modes
> 
> ### Full (default)
> Systematic exploration. Visit every reachable page. Document 5-10 well-evidenced issues. Produce health score. Takes 5-15 minutes depending on app size.
> 
> ### Quick (`--quick`)
> 30-second smoke test. Visit homepage + top 5 navigation targets. Check: page loads? Console errors? Broken links? Produce health score. No detailed issue documentation.
> 
> ### Regression (`--regression <baseline>`)
> Run full mode, then load `baseline.json` from a previous run. Diff: which issues are fixed? Which are new? What's the score delta? Append regression section to report.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Workflow
> 
> ### Phase 1: Initialize
> 
> 1. Find browse binary (see Setup above)
> 2. Create output directories
> 3. Copy report template from `qa/templates/qa-report-template.md` to output dir
> 4. Start timer for duration tracking
> 
> ### Phase 2: Authenticate (if needed)
> 
> **If the user specified auth credentials:**
> 
> ```bash
> $B goto <login-url>
> $B snapshot -i                    # find the login form
> $B fill @e3 "user@example.com"
> $B fill @e4 "[REDACTED]"         # NEVER include real passwords in report
> $B click @e5                      # submit
> $B snapshot -D                    # verify login succeeded
> ```
> 
> **If the user provided a cookie file:**
> 
> ```bash
> $B cookie-import cookies.json
> $B goto <target-url>
> ```
> 
> **If 2FA/OTP is required:** Ask the user for the code and wait.
> 
> **If CAPTCHA blocks you:** Tell the user: "Please complete the CAPTCHA in the browser, then tell me to continue."
> 
> ### Phase 3: Orient
> 
> Get a map of the application:
> 
> ```bash
> $B goto <target-url>
> $B snapshot -i -a -o "$REPORT_DIR/screenshots/initial.png"
> $B links                          # map navigation structure
> $B console --errors               # any errors on landing?
> ```
> 
> **Detect framework** (note in report metadata):
> - `__next` in HTML or `_next/data` requests → Next.js
> - `csrf-token` meta tag → Rails
> - `wp-content` in URLs → WordPress
> - Client-side routing with no page reloads → SPA
> 
> **For SPAs:** The `links` command may return few results because navigation is client-side. Use `snapshot -i` to find nav elements (buttons, menu items) instead.
> 
> ### Phase 4: Explore
> 
> Visit pages systematically. At each page:
> 
> ```bash
> $B goto <page-url>
> $B snapshot -i -a -o "$REPORT_DIR/screenshots/page-name.png"
> $B console --errors
> ```
> 
> Then follow the **per-page exploration checklist** (see `qa/references/issue-taxonomy.md`):
> 
> 1. **Visual scan** — Look at the annotated screenshot for layout issues
> 2. **Interactive elements** — Click buttons, links, controls. Do they work?
> 3. **Forms** — Fill and submit. Test empty, invalid, edge cases
> 4. **Navigation** — Check all paths in and out
> 5. **States** — Empty state, loading, error, overflow
> 6. **Console** — Any new JS errors after interactions?
> 7. **Responsiveness** — Check mobile viewport if relevant:
>    ```bash
>    $B viewport 375x812
>    $B screenshot "$REPORT_DIR/screenshots/page-mobile.png"
>    $B viewport 1280x720
>    ```
> 
> **Depth judgment:** Spend more time on core features (homepage, dashboard, checkout, search) and less on secondary pages (about, terms, privacy).
> 
> **Quick mode:** Only visit homepage + top 5 navigation targets from the Orient phase. Skip the per-page checklist — just check: loads? Console errors? Broken links visible?
> 
> ### Phase 5: Document
> 
> Document each issue **immediately when found** — don't batch them.
> 
> **Two evidence tiers:**
> 
> **Interactive bugs** (broken flows, dead buttons, form failures):
> 1. Take a screenshot before the action
> 2. Perform the action
> 3. Take a screenshot showing the result
> 4. Use `snapshot -D` to show what changed
> 5. Write repro steps referencing screenshots
> 
> ```bash
> $B screenshot "$REPORT_DIR/screenshots/issue-001-step-1.png"
> $B click @e5
> $B screenshot "$REPORT_DIR/screenshots/issue-001-result.png"
> $B snapshot -D
> ```
> 
> **Static bugs** (typos, layout issues, missing images):
> 1. Take a single annotated screenshot showing the problem
> 2. Describe what's wrong
> 
> ```bash
> $B snapshot -i -a -o "$REPORT_DIR/screenshots/issue-002.png"
> ```
> 
> **Write each issue to the report immediately** using the template format from `qa/templates/qa-report-template.md`.
> 
> ### Phase 6: Wrap Up
> 
> 1. **Compute health score** using the rubric below
> 2. **Write "Top 3 Things to Fix"** — the 3 highest-severity issues
> 3. **Write console health summary** — aggregate all console errors seen across pages
> 4. **Update severity counts** in the summary table
> 5. **Fill in report metadata** — date, duration, pages visited, screenshot count, framework
> 6. **Save baseline** — write `baseline.json` with:
>    ```json
>    {
>      "date": "YYYY-MM-DD",
>      "url": "<target>",
>      "healthScore": N,
>      "issues": [{ "id": "ISSUE-001", "title": "...", "severity": "...", "category": "..." }],
>      "categoryScores": { "console": N, "links": N, ... }
>    }
>    ```
> 
> **Regression mode:** After writing the report, load the baseline file. Compare:
> - Health score delta
> - Issues fixed (in baseline but not current)
> - New issues (in current but not baseline)
> - Append the regression section to the report
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Health Score Rubric
> 
> Compute each category score (0-100), then take the weighted average.
> 
> ### Console (weight: 15%)
> - 0 errors → 100
> - 1-3 errors → 70
> - 4-10 errors → 40
> - 10+ errors → 10
> 
> ### Links (weight: 10%)
> - 0 broken → 100
> - Each broken link → -15 (minimum 0)
> 
> ### Per-Category Scoring (Visual, Functional, UX, Content, Performance, Accessibility)
> Each category starts at 100. Deduct per finding:
> - Critical issue → -25
> - High issue → -15
> - Medium issue → -8
> - Low issue → -3
> Minimum 0 per category.
> 
> ### Weights
> | Category | Weight |
> |----------|--------|
> | Console | 15% |
> | Links | 10% |
> | Visual | 10% |
> | Functional | 20% |
> | UX | 15% |
> | Performance | 10% |
> | Content | 5% |
> | Accessibility | 15% |
> 
> ### Final Score
> `score = Σ (category_score × weight)`
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Framework-Specific Guidance
> 
> ### Next.js
> - Check console for hydration errors (`Hydration failed`, `Text content did not match`)
> - Monitor `_next/data` requests in network — 404s indicate broken data fetching
> - Test client-side navigation (click links, don't just `goto`) — catches routing issues
> - Check for CLS (Cumulative Layout Shift) on pages with dynamic content
> 
> ### Rails
> - Check for N+1 query warnings in console (if development mode)
> - Verify CSRF token presence in forms
> - Test Turbo/Stimulus integration — do page transitions work smoothly?
> - Check for flash messages appearing and dismissing correctly
> 
> ### WordPress
> - Check for plugin conflicts (JS errors from different plugins)
> - Verify admin bar visibility for logged-in users
> - Test REST API endpoints (`/wp-json/`)
> - Check for mixed content warnings (common with WP)
> 
> ### General SPA (React, Vue, Angular)
> - Use `snapshot -i` for navigation — `links` command misses client-side routes
> - Check for stale state (navigate away and back — does data refresh?)
> - Test browser back/forward — does the app handle history correctly?
> - Check for memory leaks (monitor console after extended use)
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Important Rules
> 
> 1. **Repro is everything.** Every issue needs at least one screenshot. No exceptions.
> 2. **Verify before documenting.** Retry the issue once to confirm it's reproducible, not a fluke.
> 3. **Never include credentials.** Write `[REDACTED]` for passwords in repro steps.
> 4. **Write incrementally.** Append each issue to the report as you find it. Don't batch.
> 5. **Never read source code.** Test as a user, not a developer.
> 6. **Check console after every interaction.** JS errors that don't surface visually are still bugs.
> 7. **Test like a user.** Use realistic data. Walk through complete workflows end-to-end.
> 8. **Depth over breadth.** 5-10 well-documented issues with evidence > 20 vague descriptions.
> 9. **Never delete output files.** Screenshots and reports accumulate — that's intentional.
> 10. **Use `snapshot -C` for tricky UIs.** Finds clickable divs that the accessibility tree misses.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Output Structure
> 
> ```
> .gstack/qa-reports/
> ├── qa-report-{domain}-{YYYY-MM-DD}.md    # Structured report
> ├── screenshots/
> │   ├── initial.png                        # Landing page annotated screenshot
> │   ├── issue-001-step-1.png               # Per-issue evidence
> │   ├── issue-001-result.png
> │   └── ...
> └── baseline.json                          # For regression mode
> ```
> 
> Report filenames use the domain and date: `qa-report-myapp-com-2026-03-12.md`
>

**2026-03-27 05:59:01 UTC**

**2026-03-27 05:59:01 UTC**
> Implement the following plan:
> 
> # Plan: You.md Skill System — Identity-Aware Agent Skills
> 
> ## Context
> 
> Houston wants to build a skill system for You.md that combines:
> 1. **The Library** (github.com/disler/the-library) — a catalog-based meta-skill for distributing skills/agents/prompts across projects
> 2. **You.md's identity context protocol** — voice, preferences, directives that travel across agents
> 3. **Meta-improvement** — agents improve their own context files based on what works
> 
> **Core insight:** The identity bundle IS the user's agent configuration. Skills that reference identity data (`{{voice.overall}}`, `{{preferences.agent}}`) become instantly personalized. A developer running `youmd skill init-project` in any new repo gets CLAUDE.md, project-context/, and preferred skills pre-configured from their identity — zero manual setup.
> 
> **Target audience:** AI SaaS founders who code AND create content. Developers first, content creators second.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Architecture: Build Native, Borrow Patterns
> 
> **Build native within youmd CLI.** The Library is pure markdown (no runtime code to fork). You.md needs TypeScript for identity interpolation, privacy scoping, and version-controlled sync. Borrow The Library's catalog format (YAML), SKILL.md conventions, and reference-based distribution model.
> 
> **What You.md adds over The Library:**
> - Identity-aware template variables (`{{voice.overall}}`, `{{directives.agent}}`)
> - Privacy scoping (shared/project/private) with isolation guarantees
> - Content-hash version control on synced data (already built)
> - Real CLI (`npx youmd skill install`) + slash command access
> - Cross-project sync that propagates identity changes without leaking project data
> - Meta-improvement feedback loop
> 
> ---
> 
> ## File Structure
> 
> ### New CLI files:
> ```
> cli/src/commands/skill.ts           # Subcommand router (pattern: project.ts)
> cli/src/lib/skills.ts               # Core engine: install, resolve, render, sync
> cli/src/lib/skill-catalog.ts        # YAML catalog parser/writer
> cli/src/lib/skill-renderer.ts       # Identity interpolation ({{var}} → value)
> ```
> 
> ### New skill files (ship out of the box):
> ```
> you-agent/skills/claude-md-generator.md    # Generate CLAUDE.md from identity
> you-agent/skills/project-context-init.md   # Scaffold project-context/ pattern
> you-agent/skills/voice-sync.md             # Sync voice across tools
> you-agent/skills/meta-improve.md           # Agent self-improvement protocol
> ```
> 
> ### User's global directory:
> ```
> ~/.youmd/skills/
> ├── youmd-skills.yaml          # Skill catalog
> ├── skill-metrics.json         # Usage tracking
> ├── claude-md-generator/SKILL.md
> ├── project-context-init/SKILL.md
> └── ...
> ```
> 
> ### Per-project:
> ```
> .youmd/skills/                  # Project-scoped skill overrides
> .claude/skills/youmd/           # Symlinked for Claude Code
> .cursor/rules/youmd.md          # Generated for Cursor
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Catalog Format: youmd-skills.yaml
> 
> ```yaml
> version: 1
> owner: houstongolden
> 
> skills:
>   - name: claude-md-generator
>     description: "Generate CLAUDE.md from identity + project detection"
>     version: "1.0.0"
>     source: "github:houstongolden/youmd/you-agent/skills/claude-md-generator.md"
>     scope: shared                       # shared | project | private
>     identity_fields:                    # Which identity data this skill uses
>       - preferences.agent
>       - directives.agent
>       - voice.overall
>     requires: []
>     installed: true
> ```
> 
> **Key extensions over The Library:** `scope` (propagation control), `identity_fields` (privacy whitelist), `owner` (you.md account link).
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Skill Format: SKILL.md with Identity Variables
> 
> ```markdown
> ---
> name: claude-md-generator
> version: 1.0.0
> scope: shared
> identity_fields: [preferences.agent, directives.agent, voice.overall]
> ---
> 
> # claude-md-generator
> 
> Generate a CLAUDE.md for the current project, pre-loaded with your identity.
> 
> ## Identity Context (resolved at install time)
> - **Agent preferences:** {{preferences.agent}}
> - **Directives:** {{directives.agent}}
> - **Voice:** {{voice.overall}}
> 
> ## What This Skill Does
> 1. Detect project type (package.json, Cargo.toml, etc.)
> 2. Read existing CLAUDE.md or project-context/
> 3. Generate CLAUDE.md with identity + detected project info
> 4. Write file (merge, don't overwrite)
> ```
> 
> The `{{var}}` template variables resolve against the user's live identity bundle at install/use time.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## CLI Commands
> 
> ```
> youmd skill                     # Help + installed skills summary
> youmd skill list                # Full catalog with install status
> youmd skill install <name>      # Pull from source to global dir
> youmd skill use <name>          # Run a skill (interpolate + execute)
> youmd skill remove <name>       # Remove from installation
> youmd skill sync                # Re-pull all + re-interpolate identity
> youmd skill add <name> <source> # Register new entry in catalog
> youmd skill push <name>         # Push local changes back to source
> youmd skill init-project        # Compound: CLAUDE.md + project-context + link
> youmd skill link <agent>        # Symlink to .claude/skills/, .cursor/rules/, etc.
> youmd skill improve             # Meta-improvement: review metrics, propose changes
> youmd skill metrics             # Usage stats and effectiveness scores
> ```
> 
> **`skill init-project`** is the killer DX command — runs in any new repo:
> 1. Installs claude-md-generator + project-context-init
> 2. Generates CLAUDE.md from identity
> 3. Scaffolds project-context/
> 4. Symlinks to .claude/skills/
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Cross-Project Sync Protocol
> 
> **Trigger:** `youmd push`, `youmd pull`, or `youmd skill sync`
> 
> 1. **Detect change** — compare identity content hash against last known
> 2. **Find affected skills** — filter catalog by `identity_fields` overlap with changed fields
> 3. **Re-interpolate** — re-resolve `{{var}}` templates against current identity data
> 4. **Respect scope** — shared propagates everywhere, project stays local, private never syncs
> 
> **Isolation guarantees:**
> - **Shared:** voice, preferences, directives, standards → propagates to all projects
> - **Project:** PRD, TODO, decisions, project-specific agent instructions → stays in project
> - **Private:** API keys, vault, internal links → never leaves the device
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Phases
> 
> ### Phase 1: Foundation (build first)
> - `cli/src/commands/skill.ts` — subcommand router
> - `cli/src/lib/skill-catalog.ts` — YAML read/write
> - `cli/src/lib/skills.ts` — install, remove, list
> - Register `skill` command in `cli/src/index.ts`
> - Write `claude-md-generator.md` + `project-context-init.md` skills

> Base directory for this skill: /Users/houstongolden/.claude/skills/browse
> 
> # browse: QA Testing & Dogfooding
> 
> Persistent headless Chromium. First call auto-starts (~3s), then ~100ms per command.
> State persists between calls (cookies, tabs, login sessions).
> 
> ## Core QA Patterns
> 
> ### 1. Verify a page loads correctly
> ```bash
> $B goto https://yourapp.com
> $B text                          # content loads?
> $B console                       # JS errors?
> $B network                       # failed requests?
> $B is visible ".main-content"    # key elements present?
> ```
> 
> ### 2. Test a user flow
> ```bash
> $B goto https://app.com/login
> $B snapshot -i                   # see all interactive elements
> $B fill @e3 "user@test.com"
> $B fill @e4 "password"
> $B click @e5                     # submit
> $B snapshot -D                   # diff: what changed after submit?
> $B is visible ".dashboard"       # success state present?
> ```
> 
> ### 3. Verify an action worked
> ```bash
> $B snapshot                      # baseline
> $B click @e3                     # do something
> $B snapshot -D                   # unified diff shows exactly what changed
> ```
> 
> ### 4. Visual evidence for bug reports
> ```bash
> $B snapshot -i -a -o /tmp/annotated.png   # labeled screenshot
> $B screenshot /tmp/bug.png                # plain screenshot
> $B console                                # error log
> ```
> 
> ### 5. Find all clickable elements (including non-ARIA)
> ```bash
> $B snapshot -C                   # finds divs with cursor:pointer, onclick, tabindex
> $B click @c1                     # interact with them
> ```
> 
> ### 6. Assert element states
> ```bash
> $B is visible ".modal"
> $B is enabled "#submit-btn"
> $B is disabled "#submit-btn"
> $B is checked "#agree-checkbox"
> $B is editable "#name-field"
> $B is focused "#search-input"
> $B js "document.body.textContent.includes('Success')"
> ```
> 
> ### 7. Test responsive layouts
> ```bash
> $B responsive /tmp/layout        # mobile + tablet + desktop screenshots
> $B viewport 375x812              # or set specific viewport
> $B screenshot /tmp/mobile.png
> ```
> 
> ### 8. Test file uploads
> ```bash
> $B upload "#file-input" /path/to/file.pdf
> $B is visible ".upload-success"
> ```
> 
> ### 9. Test dialogs
> ```bash
> $B dialog-accept "yes"           # set up handler
> $B click "#delete-button"        # trigger dialog
> $B dialog                        # see what appeared
> $B snapshot -D                   # verify deletion happened
> ```
> 
> ### 10. Compare environments
> ```bash
> $B diff https://staging.app.com https://prod.app.com
> ```
> 
> ## Snapshot Flags
> 
> ```
> -i        Interactive elements only (buttons, links, inputs)
> -c        Compact (no empty structural nodes)
> -d <N>    Limit depth
> -s <sel>  Scope to CSS selector
> -D        Diff against previous snapshot
> -a        Annotated screenshot with ref labels
> -o <path> Output path for screenshot
> -C        Cursor-interactive elements (@c refs)
> ```
> 
> Combine: `$B snapshot -i -a -C -o /tmp/annotated.png`
> 
> Use @refs after snapshot: `$B click @e3`, `$B fill @e4 "value"`, `$B click @c1`
> 
> ## Full Command List
> 
> **Navigate:** goto, back, forward, reload, url
> **Read:** text, html, links, forms, accessibility
> **Snapshot:** snapshot (with flags above)
> **Interact:** click, fill, select, hover, type, press, scroll, wait, wait --networkidle, wait --load, viewport, upload, cookie-import, dialog-accept, dialog-dismiss
> **Inspect:** js, eval, css, attrs, is, console, console --errors, network, dialog, cookies, storage, perf
> **Visual:** screenshot, pdf, responsive
> **Compare:** diff
> **Multi-step:** chain (pipe JSON array)
> **Tabs:** tabs, tab, newtab, closetab
> **Server:** status, stop, restart
> 
> 
> ARGUMENTS: https://you.md
